After curing it until it is healed.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	Of the pustule which is called "Thelul"
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you are working with the shoulder bone, if it seems to be one and a half inches in size, heat up the cautery that looks like two blades, then place it completely heated on the coped shoulder; keep your hand with the cautery until it reaches the beginning of the vein from which blood flows. Do this once or twice, and if there are many shoulder bones, cauterize each one as we have said; after the treatment for beneficial ointments is done when they are healthy. And if you cauterize with a large-sized cautery, it will provide more assistance.
de plaie mal curee	from a poorly treated wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient is unable to endure a cut or opening, as we will detail in its section, if such sickness occurs that cannot be healed except by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont. Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou .ij. ou .iij., selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes. se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	When a certain opening does not come about and is aged with putrefaction and corrupted moisture, if you need to try the entire process once carefully, be sure that you know precisely how much the attempt has progressed. Heat up the cautery to resemble a blade of .i., then place it in the opening according to the quantity that this attempt has entered into, and continue using the cautery until the infected, putrefied parts are charred completely, once, or twice, or three times, depending on your need; be cautious not to burn the nerves and the major veins. If the opening went into the bladder's body and towards the intestine, be aware of these points, and do this only in a place where it will not harm. After healing the place until it is healthy, and when the pus has been absorbed over a long period, then you can ascertain that the process was complete; and if the materials have not been absorbed, know that there's still pus inside, and the bone has become corroded at the bottom; thus as with one of these we will speak about in its place.
de la maladie des reins	Regarding kidney illness
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When abdominal pain stems from the kidneys and accompanied by large wind movements, it affects women in particular cases, thus you should apply a cautery to both sides of the kidneys and to the arm where we previously mentioned; and if we cauterize it at the center, we would perform three cauterizations in line, which will provide more assistance.
de la vessie	From the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is diseased and weak from heat and moisture, so that the patient retains urine, then one should apply a cautery to the lower part of the bladder, where hair begins on the penis, and one each on the right and left side, and each cautery should be as long as your finger. And you do one application of a cautery behind the back, or two if needed; and let the cautery resemble a small spoon in shape as previously described.
de la marris	From the maris (maris is likely misspelled for "mânes" which means souls)
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the manes are cold and moist, and do not allow for conception, and the flowers become corrupted and their ends delay; and when they come forth, one can feel great pain: thus it is fitting that you apply three cauterizations inside the womb, as we have instructed for the bladder or fire cautery, and two cauterizations behind the back; and let the cauterizations resemble a small spoon, as we have described.
de la hainche	From the hip
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the viscous fluids descend in the cavity of the hip, and due to this reason it moves out of its place, and the signs are that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and the joints can be found from their origin, so you should cauterize the hair on the cavity of the hip with about one fire cautery resembling a circle, and mark in front of the joint inside the cavity as it turns, so that the cavity is within the circle; and have your cauteries like those used to cauterize the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you don't have those fire cauteries handy, make three olive-sized large fire cauteries, and ensure that all the points of these are as well-made as the rest. And treat it until there is no pain.
de la dolor de la hainche	Regarding hip pain
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes to the hip joint, and this is due to coldness and moisture, and the patient is treated as we have described in the division, but the cure is ineffective, and the illness is old: then it is necessary that you cleanse the patient of large fluids using bad-smelling pills, or other similar good pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu. Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche .iij. cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a .iiij. selonc ceste forme:	After performing the cauterization; and the way of cauterization is according to two methods: this means mixing hot medicines, and cauterizing with fire. The fire cauterizer can be done in several ways, among which one method is: you should cauterize at the hip joint with three triangular cauterizations following this form, and each has a good depth and size, and there's space the size of a coin between each cauterization, and these are olive cauterizations; no cauterization is done in the middle above the main part of the hip joint, because there are four like this:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see that you need to cauterize at the circular cauterizer as we have mentioned before in the dislocation of the hip joint; but do it in such a way that the circles contain all the hip joint, and all the parts of the blood are burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe. Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai .ij. cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et .i. cautere desus la cheville .iiij. dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor .iij. poins ou .iiij. au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And this is the way to treat sciatica, when pain stays in the hip, and doesn't reach up to the thigh or leg. And if it reaches up to the thigh and leg, then we make two cauterizations there where the pain stays, and one above the ankle on the third day, at the left part a little bit; and have the cauterizations done with surgical knives, and burn away any thickened flesh from the wound; and should the patient feel that the pain extends up to about four inches down or near it, then cauterize where they sense the pain three points or four at the cauterization known as 'points'.
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if the job requires more; and should it be that the pain is from above the knee towards the thigh, then make cauterization with a surgical knife or circular cautery. And ensure you take great care in all your cauterizations not to leave any part of the process undone, burning nerves and large arteries as well while ensuring no unnecessary harm and contraction are caused to the patient.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez. Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	And I myself have seen several who had made a cauterization up to the ankle bone, and left them so that the leg was swollen all the way down, and also the joints, causing them to become inflamed and rotten. After this stomach treatment, they died.
Et se li dolors est en .ij. parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere. // Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai .i. tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de .ij. pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait .i. mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And if the pains are in two parts together, apply cautery to both, according to this manner. // And as for the physician's advice on the fire cautery of the hip, which is described here, do as follows: make one such iron rod and have it at the top also as thick as a young hare's foot or perhaps slightly smaller, and place them in between with one iron rod placed among the other right up to the distance of the space of a nut; and let there be the iron rods opposite both parts, and they should resemble knots, and have two iron handles well made; and this is the form:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And heat it until it becomes completely red and steam starts to rise, then place the heated iron on the spot of the hip ailment, and twist it over the healthy side. And apply the cauterization once with one iron rod and leave for three days; and after that, apply a dressing of butter, and keep the wound open for as long as possible; finish the ointment treatment until it becomes clean.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we use very little of this cautery for the fear of his judgment, and we see few who use it; however, such is a good cautery which one can endure, and leave where it settles.
de la dolor dou dos	Of the pain of the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether by falling or impact, or too much evacuation, or through exposure to cold matter, none of these conditions warrant cauterization, for it is akin to that which arises from an infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	After ensuring that the patient's body is free of foul pills or other similar symptoms, one should apply treatments to the back, at the site where the pain resides, three lines marked with a cross, and in each line up to five cauterizations depending on how much and how intensely the body can endure; perform the cauterization using the cauterization method known as "points"; and if you see fit, do three or four cauterizations halfway between the cauterization for the clavicle according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	This illness often affects small children, and the signs of its beginning are that they seem pale when they stand up, and fear; you find it in the last spinal cord at the back and we see the appearance coming on other spinal cords.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and observe its treatment,
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument. Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant .ij. lignes ou .iij., et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	So that the cautery touches each part of the spine equally. And if you observe this, apply the hot cautery to the spine in two or three lines,
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain in joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When joint pain is due to moisture that spreads throughout the body, and when pain comes in the foot, they call it "gout" properly, and when it's caused by cold and cannot be cured with medicine, it should be treated using cauteries in this manner: make a fire cautery inside the joint of the foot, and let the cautery use olive oil according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point». Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if there is need that you grasp on the face of the foot, make him undergo cautery across all the cautery saying 'point'. And if the pains come up to the knees and other joints, and this happens many times, then make him undergo cautery on each knee. Three or four in every part, across all the olive oil cautery; and if you need more, do so accordingly, but don't remove your hand until the heat is fully gone from the wound.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre. Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile .ij. lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines. Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	And if the pains descend to the knees and back, he should be given the cautery as we have mentioned in this chapter. And if the pains are at the hands, then make points between the fingers four lines deep; and if there is no pain left on the back, then make points on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come to the elbows or shoulders, then cauterize each part, and take good care of him and administer medicines. For if you give him good care and purge phlegm, he will be healed with the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	Regarding the rupture of the uterus
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When rupture comes about in the lungs, and the bowels descend to the kidneys, this is newly happening. It's necessary that when you look at them being cured, they don't eat anything during that day; and they should use things that lighten the stomach, so that the wind descends from their belly. After have them sit up on their back between your hands, then command him to cut his arm until the intestines are repaired, and bring it back with your fingers, and feel for under the rupture upon the bone of the wrist, and do all at a sign as if it were half a circle above the chest; then heat the cautery that is described here:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles. Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui .i. cussin et .i. serjant sus les cuisses, et .i. autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Until it is white and gives off fumes. Then bring the bowels back to their place; and let the attendants cut his hand so they do not turn around; and work well on the thighs with the patient, and put a cushion under each thigh and another under his buttocks which touch your hands; then place the cautery at the mark all over your hand, and hold one steady and the other straight until you reach the bone, and if you don't reach it the first time, keep repeating this until you reach the bone; and watch carefully that the intestines do not slip when you make the heat; that you don't burn them; and that because of this the patient does not suffer, or any other harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien. Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés .iij. jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides .xl. jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And know that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your work is for nothing. It's necessary that the children's cauteries be subtle according to their size and the large people's also be as large according to their measure; after three days treat his arm with butter under the cautery until the scab is removed; afterwards treat other ointments until it heals properly, and let the patient lie on his back for forty days so that the wound is well healed; and it must be that his bedridden times are long enough so that the intestines do not slip when he wishes to go to chambers.
Et aprés .xl. jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse .xl. autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement. Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And after forty days, when he wishes to stand up, he should apply a well-made bandage and keep it on for forty more days; with good rest, he must work moderately and refrain from excessive drinking and eating, as well as loud shouting; once this instruction is followed, they are completely cured. And I will later explain the treatment of cutting in my chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the rupture of the abdomen
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai .j. cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a .iij. angles selonc ceste forme:	When ruptures occur in other bellies and are known, if you notice that they no longer grow, then apply the fire cautery according to their quantity, taking one-third of the thumb; after that, treat it as we have instructed. And none of the old ones said that one should cauterize with the three-cornered firebrand in this shape:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile. Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	The first sign is the location of entry and make a line across the width above the wound, and another below, and guide your hand with all the fire cautery. But the first cauterizations are lighter and wetter.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	from ancient pain in no limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor. s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence .i. autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	When pain comes to any limb, whether from falling or being hit, and if this pain lasts long, and medicine does not cure it, then it should be cauterized with a cautery called "point", and the applications of the cauteries must correspond to the length of the limb and its smallness and weakness and its function and its location in relation to twists and pain. If the first application is effective, that's good; if not, apply another one after this, for such things usually cause it to move near the body part they are closest to, so you should perform the cauterizations until the patient feels relief.
de meselerie	In mixture
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie. Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai .v. cauteres sus lou chief: .i. emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et .ij. sus les .ij. cornes, et .i. derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	The mixtures are treated with a cautery on multiple occasions and also the disease that arises from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy. If you see them being cauterized, take care if the disease is in the beginning stage and when it is cured according to what we have said in the division section, not letting it reoccur or persist, and if there are doubts that corruption spreads throughout the diseased part then do this: apply four times with the cautery. The first one begins at the head and goes towards the nose after nine steps; and another one is made from the head to the end of the hairline; and two others on the two horns, and one behind on the neck; and keep your hand so that the cautery reaches up to the bone, until the scabs come out entirely allowing for the fumes of the thick humors to escape; and cauterize it on the mouse area as is done before.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the mixture is everywhere spread out and it's clearly apparent, then it's necessary that you cauterize with these cauteries that we've mentioned on the head and one cautery in the middle of the nose, and two cauteries on the spine from the neck to the back, and six on the spine from the shoulder blades down, and one large on the knee and another slightly smaller, and two on each shoulder blade; and two on the ribs, and two on the tendons of the foot, and one on each joint of hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and be careful not to burn any nerves that are under the back part of the heel, do not burn them. And never cauterize near the bone in the elbow, and another one near the bone of the stomach, and one near the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus. Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers. Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	And know that the more I use the cautery, the more help it provides, and it benefits them; and know that patients do not feel pain during cautery as healthy people do, for their bodies are already completely corrupted. And ensure that the cautery sizes are large or small according to limbs and joints, just like you will find in descriptions of metalwork techniques. After treatment, dust the area several times with honey and other remedies until it heals.
de enfleure	Of inflation
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez. Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	When swelling appears in any limb and is treated with medicines, oils, and bandages, but does not heal, then you should make a cautery on the limb according to its size; and make sure that the cautery enters only slightly into the inner flesh of the wound. Then treat it with poultices until it heals. And one should apply the cautery both above and below the wrist and ankle, along the exit point of the nerves that paralyze the limb, and in this way remove the swelling; and yet no one should interfere unless they are knowledgeable about limbs and the exits of moving body nerves.
de albaras	Of cauteries by fire, command the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they pierce at their base, hold the eyes still so they do not move until they grow.
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" has worsened, and medical remedies are of no use, then use a small cautery to cauterize, according to the size of the lesion, until the pus is removed and its color changes; then cleanse with flour mixed with lentils, rose oil, and plantain leaves, as well as blood from colognes and almond birds, each in their part. Mix all together, wrap it with a cloth, apply it to the affected area until it heals.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The treatment of gangrene by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble .i. cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.  Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	When the ulcer starts to appear at the beginning, and you see it stopping, if you stop it by applying the cautery, do so around a circle, all around the edge of the ulcer. And sometimes they advise that you apply the cautery in the middle of the ulcer; and oftentimes this does not seem right to me because I fear it might cause it to be ulcerated and corrupted, something I've seen happen before. A more straightforward approach is to apply the cautery around it, using the circle-shaped cautery we spoke of earlier.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	Of the swelling that cannot die.

Car elle se hastera de meureir.	When someone has a disease called "adubelati", and it doesn't die off or because of the excess it causes or due to the old age of the illness when it is decrepit (that is, too old), and there's little blood left in the body, or due to its strength; and you see that it needs to die faster: then apply small cauteries around in several places; leave it like this. For it will hasten to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it pierced through with all of the cautery tool, if you heat up this form of the cautery that is described:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis. Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement. li cure dou feu par fer	The cure by fire using a iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches. Et puis le laisse .iij. jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption. Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.  Et se tu vois aprés .iij. jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus. Another method for disease involves what is called 'corrosion', and this is nothing more than limb damage, because it affects the limbs just like one might burn dry wood. If you observe this disease on the body that can withstand a combined cautery of fire, then make small and large clavicular cauterizations according to where the disease resides; after applying cauterization from all sides until you remove all corruption, leaving nothing behind - ensure everything corrupt is extracted. And then leave it for three days. Apply a burn with oil on the cauterized areas until any scabbing from the heat has been healed and all corruption is gone. After this ointment cure of generating flesh. And if after three days healthy tissue hasn't started to grow, that's good; but if not, restart the fire cautery on what remains of the corrupted area. This damage can sometimes be treated with medicine in place of a fire cautery; however, fire cautery is more effective aid and I have previously discussed this medicine cure in the division: take it when you need to do so.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	From stones that come into joints
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet. Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times, a disease occurs in bones that originates from within which is called 'cyst' according to our understanding, and this is a large, solid lump that hurts the bone. The cauterization for this disease can be done in two ways: fire cautery and hot water cautery.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines. And if they have been moved from beneath the body, and often occur in hands and limbs, it is necessary that you bring them the cautery of hot water; and thus: take one of an arane's hair or iron, or a feather of goose, and place them on the nail and the althelul, meaning for warts; and place the stick so that it touches all around, then put a bit of hot water, hold your hand well, press your hand back in such a way that the edge of the stick burns to the base of the nail, and then find the deep passage of hot water down to the base; and let the patient endure the hot water burn for a little while an hour; then leave them like this, and it will be uprooted from all its roots. Do this one after another until you are done with those on your body, then treat any swellings that generate flesh.

des pustules puans	of the pus-filled sores

quant li artere est copee	when the artery has been tied
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times there have been great flows of blood from the artery that has been tied at the wound, or during an incision on an abscess, or during the cauterization of a limb, and similar incidents; it is very distressing to smell this.

Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it jumps out when you lift your finger from the vein, and the cauteries are heated, take quickly one more of the cauteries that are hot.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not stop doing this one after another until the skin becomes cool; and watch that you don't burn the nerve underneath it, and that no harm comes to the patient; and know that when the skin is cut off from the artery, one can hardly properly cool it themselves when the artery is large, unless it's through one of the four methods we have mentioned: by cautery, or extraction if it wasn't treated yet, or with strong string application, or by applying medicine that has the power to cool blood; and tie and hold in place for future use.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who will administer treatment by tightly binding with cloths or by placing burning objects thereupon, or other similar things, if it doesn't benefit then do not proceed.

And if this happens to anyone and they have no sight or medicine at hand, if they must apply their index finger onto the wound of the vein as we said earlier, stretch it well so that it remains stuck under the wound and under the vein; and do not move it, but moisten it with cold water often until it is very cold. And create gaps in front of those who need cautery and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	This begins the second book on treatments for wounds.

And I advise you not to undertake folly. For many ways of people come in treatments. And from these I give you the meaning and say: "Wait, I am a doctor"; and the disease is stubborn. dou chief plein d’aigue	The head full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this disease comes about very often in infants at birth, and when the mother presses too hard on the baby's head; and sometimes it happens due to no other reason than we don't know.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I never see this disease outside of infants, and among all those that I have seen their death hastened; and for this reason it seems to me worth abandoning the practice of such treatments.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw one child of this, where the shoulder was full of water, and their head swelled each day until it could no longer be supported; and because of so much moisture he died, and this moisture is assembled around the bone under the elbow, between the chest and the bone; and the treatments are such that if the moisture is within the chest and the bone, and the abscesses are small, you make a large cut across the head; and let it be as long as two hands, as long as the moisture runs; and see this form of spasm:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	When moisture accumulates more, and if the abscess is bigger, make two incisions in a manner like a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if moisture is under the bone, and you see the corners of the forehead opening on each side, and a sharp pain occurs when you press it from your hand internally, and this does not respond: then it must be that you cut through the center of the forehead with three cuts according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers. Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	And after making the incision, extract all moisture outside. After treating the cuts with bandages and powders, put wine and oil and leave like this until the fifth day; then remove it, treat the wound by changing dressings and ointments, and allow the head to rest equally, and afterwards give the patient dry meat from the inner moist area until the member is strengthened and healthy.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way of incision is that you look at where the aperture of the abscess opens, and the assembly of the water; for it never stands in front; nor behind; nor to the right; and never to the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	So cut the place where the abscess opens and the water filling it, make a cut according to your ability and watch that you do not cut the artery; look for a source of blood, so that the patient dies from the flow of blood and the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	regarding remedies
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When it comes to any illness that is called "catarrh" either around the eyes or at the bottom of the nose, and this sickness is old, and medical treatment does not help, then the last resort treatment involves cauterization using what one would cut off their two main arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout .i. drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de .ij. pars. tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	It is necessary then, as you see fit, that the patient bend their head; after this, rub the area with a coarse cloth until the arteries are visible, then pull out the patient's throat to the length of one hand. Then observe where the vein lies and check both ears after them, noting if they have returned; then mark each ear, then cut both with a sharp knife across two parts until the size matches up to the bone, and this should be done by the width of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see this, hold the knife over the artery and cut above it, making the incision also as wide as two inches through.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, make sure to pull the string continuously upwards from there.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de .iij. dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est .vj. c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins. selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open with feeling, it is necessary that you measure the size of the space to be about three inches, then gently press and apply until reaching the bone; and what should be done regarding blood to remove is about six cubic centimeters, and by chance a little more or less depending on how well the patient can bear it, and the fullness of the artery; then look at the wound: if there remains just above the bone point of syphilis, if there is no trace of abscesses left after incision, then press the wound and tie it, and apply ointment until it heals.
de emigrainne	Of grains
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When the old age comes along and severe colds occur, due to moisture from tears and heat in the temples and elsewhere, as well as similar conditions. Medicine is treated through the methods of medicinal cures, but none of these help it much. Then we extract the veins in the temples and cauterize them, just like what we have recounted.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the method for their extraction is that one should lead the patient's hair from the temples to where the artery opens on them, as it opens well by its pulsation and responds only in those whose heads are overly cold; and if it does respond, hold the neck of the patient with some cloths, then rub the head with a rough cloth, and raise the head under hot water until the artery clearly appears; then take out the cautery tool that has this form:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des .ij. chiés. Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	Then lightly scrape the skin until you see the artery; then guide it upward with forceps and remove all tissues from each section very well; and if the artery is thin, twist it at the tip of the hook. Then cut that part according to the number of both bones. For if it is not cut properly, it will cause bleeding everywhere.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And drain out the blood until the seventh day; and if the artery is large, it's necessary that you tie it with two strands of a sturdy silk thread, so that putrefaction doesn't occur before the healing of the wound, or during bleeding; then cut away any excess material between the two threads at this very moment. And when you see fit, apply cautery from the surgical knife until the bone, as long as the bones are cut. This is the main task, should the patient not have fever and their complexion be warm.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the cauterizers are help to finish the moisture: because with them it is of greater help against moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	It is necessary for the extraction of arteries that you fill the whole with old cotton and place well-made tents above it; and when they are released, if you do a cure with dry medicines that generate pus and tents until it becomes clear; and if there's no artery bleeding then do as you work, quickly apply heat from the cauterizer, or use the whole of vitriol and squeeze it in your hand so that the blood becomes congealed; and if you don't have this on hand, fill the hand with alcohol until the blood is frozen, and dip the hand in cold water until the bleeding stops, then hold it as needed; and what is softer and more fluid during the extraction of an artery is that you cauterize the vein from this cauterized trenching at .ij. parts, but the trenching should be well spaced to keep heat for a longer time.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instruments are too tense, they retain less of their heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it should have between the two knives half an inch, and then when you have decided to insert both of them, and you place the heated iron until it reaches the bone, and cut along two lines; and keep them far apart as this cautery does not fully adhere everywhere; and this is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	Of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears from the eyes are draining through the veins that are under the skin of the head and face, and no benefit comes from medicine being applied there, you'll see the skin turn red, and feel or notice heat on the forehead as if it were pulsating; and at such places they become damp and wet so that paper hairs fall off, and the papers get heated, and are burnt by the heat of the tears, in which case this treatment is needed.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai .iij. fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com .ij. doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres .ij. as .ij. costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as .ij. costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des .ij. mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de .iij. dois au traver joins;	And they called him the old "bruise healer", and you should instruct this patient with this sickness to let their hairs grow on or above their forehead, then I will make three cuts evenly across the forehead according to its length; and have one of the cuts in the same way as two halves all along the forehead downwards until it reaches half, and the other two cuts at each side near the eyes, and be careful not to cut into the arteries that are above the eyes; and keep your hand away from joining the two halves together again, and each wound should have the width of three fingers through their join.
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de .ij. pars de coi ci est li forme:	And have an applicator of sponge and a bit of cloth to wipe away the blood, then use the sharp spit from two parts where this is formed here:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	From the cut that is behind the temple until the second cut; and remove all the flesh in between the two cuts up to the part on the bone, then continue with another cut from the middle cut until the other second one, and then remove this spit.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	if you use the tool called "cultellaire" in the first opening, and it is very sharp on one side, and blunt on the other, not sharp, and this shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure. Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place the cutting edge of the tool towards the lung's air passage at the heart, and the soft end towards the bone, and push the tool until it touches halfway through the wall. And remove all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes until the incision is continuous up to where the opening occurs at the heart, and then proceed in the middle slit until you reach the other opening; and drain equal amounts of blood, expressing the heart for the taken blood; then place a layer of old cotton in each slit, and cover with moist cloths soaked in wine and oil and basil, making sure no pus is present; and on the third day remove the stitches, and apply large quantities of water-based treatment, then continue treating with ointment made from basil and olive oil, and other treatments for wounds until healed.
dou reume des eulz	from the inflammation
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When it comes to sudden fever and habituated coughing, and you see the eyes red and small, and weakening of vision, and burned paper; and hair falls out, and one sweats profusely, and the body aches with malaria-like pains, and the patient shivers; then know through these incidents that those matters and this fever come from many veins, and the treatment given, if it is such.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large. i. poc. Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les .ij. levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And you instruct the patient about their forehead, then make a large incision through the forehead, and another wide one. Start from the left temple incision to the right temple, and ensure the cut goes down to the bone; and keep your hand away from the brain nerves that move during eating. When the bone is exposed, flush all the blood with an sponge, then clean between the two lips of the incision and place old cotton and linen fabric; afterwards, cover it with wet cloths soaked in wine and oil, taking care not to leave any remnants. Once the bone is out, you should rub it until new flesh begins to grow, then treat it with things that promote growth and healing.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take two parts of wheat flower and four parts of colofoin, and make a poultice with them; then administer it to these wounds to promote the growth of flesh everywhere.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	From the burning of ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that chokes in the ears is one of four things: grains, or animal, or mine stone or similar thing like iron; or seed, like beans, peas; or flowing substance like water and oil and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel. Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus. Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	When it chokes in the ear or with any other matter that doesn't fit into the ear or doesn't grow inside the ear, put the ear under the sun. If you see a stone, if you distill a drop of violet oil or pine resin oil, then proceed to extraction; and make them sneeze with consideration, and plug the nostrils when sneezing comes, and insert pieces of cloth or wool into the ear; and hold the ear above. Often this cure brings relief; and if it doesn't bring relief, then proceed to extraction with subtle hooks, as shown here:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it jumps out with the hooks, that's good; if not, proceed with extraction using a thin and delicate tool of small curvature; and if it doesn't jump out this way, make an araneae stick and hold the tip of the stick or the edge of the ear very firmly, plug the wax hole inside the stick as tightly as possible so that nothing can enter with the stick; then pull forcefully, for often this brings relief as we have said; and if it doesn't bring relief in such a way, take out the wax and hold any tool ready to do this work, put a little cotton in there; then press the wax or whatever is there onto the stone, and pull with force.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if she cannot heal from all these things that we have said, hurry to cut the ear in such a way that pus and phlegm escape, along with spasms; and the method of cutting is as follows: first you make an incision near the auricular muscle, draining blood according to its capacity. Then place the ear between your hands and turn the ear upwards, making a small cut at the base of the ear in the fatty part hanging down; let the cut be like a crescent moon until you reach the bone, then extract the bone with force and suck it quickly into your mouth; perform the cure while it's still clean.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if they are grains and it inflates, administer extraction; and if it cannot come out, perform this type of puncturing in such a way:
et amenistre incision de celui grain. Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	And perform an incision on that grain. But do not perform this when you think the grains are moist due to the moisture of the ear, until you have done many pieces; then remove them with fine tweezers and suck out the pus, as we said, so that the extractions become easier.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton. Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est. s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin. se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent .i. jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	In the case of weeping from the ear, then it must be that the patient uses expectoration of cold fluids first, and broadly fill the ear with old cotton. And remain lying on the same or another side where the cold is. If it leaps out through this, it's good. If not, take several stones according to their length along your desire and gently, then heat them a bit over fire; and place one or a few of these stones in his ear, and leap forward from one foot on the other, and strike with another stone on the stone that is in the ear; and do not stop this action stone by stone until all cold comes out completely, and so it leaps out completely; and if you see fit, take one, and insert a piece of the head into the ear, and the other head with fire until the most sensitive piece of the twig becomes charred; then redo another row of twigs until all cold is released, as we have spoken about in stones.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of the beast, if it is small like a flea and similar thing, treat it as we have said in division; but if there's something noticeable that one can feel, then perform the extraction with forceps; this is the lighter thing to remove in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of the twisted worms in the ears, if you're treating it as we have said in division and about distillation therapies, and if the treatment doesn't benefit, then you should examine the ear to the sun: if there is no worm visible, then treat with small forceps; and if nothing's visible, take the shape of this:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus. Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent. Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And make it tight below and loose above. And place the finest part of the curette in the ear according to the amount of suffering from the illness, then proceed to fully apply the paste; do this repeatedly until all the pus has come out. If they do not leave by themselves, numb the area inside the ear with cotton as I have said about the stone; and if they do not protrude forcefully as we have said, administer distillations that the old people have proven effective in worm removal, and you will find them or treatments for distillations; and distill your oils and medicines into the ear through this instrument, which is formed just like you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And use either silver or arsenic in a small tube below for distillation and to press within the distillation with one well-made tool of arsenic suitable for this task. And place a piece of cotton wrapped around the end extension near the raseur. Then pour your oil or juice into the tube, and observe what you see from your medicines within the wick, and have the wick in the ear; then fill the raseur completely with all the cotton, press your hand gently until the oil is fully distilled or until it has reached the ear canal; and listen to the symptoms within, and ensure that one portion of distillation is heated over fire just like you do when distilling it into the ear; and make sure it's not too cold because the medicine would not be as effective.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Regarding ear piercing or perforation.
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without any missing parts in their ears; and this same thing happens to people when there's injury or birth in the ear, and these injuries come into the ear sometimes unseen if one can't see them; and never does one have more than one hole for the ear, and one sees it very well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	That which comes unseen, if one can't see it, is of healing in multiple positions, and in that situation where one sees that you should place the ear to the sun; and look inside: if you see the apparent thickening, if the work has become this pus-like substance from which the following description is related:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And let it be so and cut in front and behind all flatly, so that it doesn't hurt the ear; if the thickening is from a birth or a part of the ear, if you have fine pincers, and gently scrape, until that flesh is entirely removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren .i. raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille. And if the operations are placed precisely in the ear, take .i. a thin and light rasp, rub it gently on fire, then place it behind the ear. des poilz des papieres	The phrase "des poilz des papieres" translates to "the hairs of paper". This could refer to thin or lightweight material that resembles hair, possibly used in various crafts or as a decorative element.

En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; puis cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	No matter how many times they are born or emerge as scorpions with different heads, some resemble pies' legs; and there are those that have a charred body with a faint color, while others have a good-colored char. For the chars that are of a good color but not charred, it is fitting to have the patient hold their hands against the sun with the malformed part facing upwards; work on their nostrils, pour vinegar onto these chars and remove them; then hold what you can bear of the fine sharp spiciness on one side until you know that this char has been fully removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains anything that we cannot cope with, should you open the wound completely using two fine and light instruments, ensuring nothing stays inside. And if it is without obstacle or abscess, if it needs to be cleaned as it should; and if it's an evil abscess, if you act quickly and use heat until all pus has drained out and all bones are clean. Then let the water or wine flow freely out of it.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, acoi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes .i. fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice .i. doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil. Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu .iij. jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	And if the nose is operated upon, and moisture comes until the palate, know that it has been cleansed; and should there be no opening or pus when you cut as intended, know that there is new flesh growing within the bone, to which neither of the instruments can come for cutting: thus it's necessary that you insert one thread of linen somewhat thick, knot it with your hands, and place between each knot an inch or less; and guide the patient so they breathe through their nose and pull out the thread as it comes out from inside the nose. Children often do this in schools, and it is a simple task for those who are to perform it; then hold one head coming out by your hand, and the other head coming out from the mouth with the other hand, knowing how they follow each other according to our instructions. Do this until you know that the knots have been rotten off the flesh, then pull out the threads, drain the blood, moisten the thread in Egyptian ointment, and reapply it in the nose as before; do this for three days or more until all of what was left from the flesh is corroded away; and then use a piece of opium for several days if they are cleansed, and if there's need for dried medicines, apply them; and that's how the tool to cleanse the head works, in which one distills oils and medicines with wine.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it should be made of silver or lead, resembling an open lamp, like a cane, and guide it that way; and if you see fit, make a closed cane, and have the instruments filled to purge the head; and hold one end of the head when heating oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	from the nose hair
