Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times the head under the nose experiences a sickness called "telul", it grows and becomes large to the point of being visible; because this requires that you start by cutting at its beginning, then remove all bone, after which place your cautery or burning medicine in it; and if you delay cutting until it is large, if it becomes hard, changes color, loses sensation: don't touch it with iron as there's an abscess inside, for when one cuts it once, it can cause great harm to the patient; and if the abscess was due to hot touch, not just change of color, and you see that all can be cut away, then empty the patient and treat the area with drying and restraining substances.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the nose is cut and sewn.
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes. Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les .ij. levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Know that when solutions of continuation come into one of these venous vessels, it benefits little, for this happens in few men. Therefore, it is necessary for this to occur in none if the wound is fresh all over with blood; and then adjust the two lips to a seam, after treating until they are clean; and should the lips be dry from one side to another, then it is necessary that you sear every part of their keratin until they heal, then bring together the two lips to a seam, and hold them tight, applying powdered dragon's blood and incense ground; and place powders on top with a piece of plaster, of strong or another soldering plaster, and leave it until it discharges by itself, then treat with ointment until they are clean.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The method of sewing is such that you join the seam: either with needles, as we have said in the abdominal stitch; or with thread, which I have made known to you.
des apostemes des levres	of the abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	In the hands of a surgeon inside a wound abscessed hard, resembling grains sometimes large and small; therefore it is necessary that you re-open the lips, cut into each nodule, and take them with tweezers in each part; then after the vitriol incision, let the wound bleed until the pus is exhausted; and then drain gently, and cure the wound of dry things until it is clean.
de la char des gencives	from the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times, a connective tissue forms on the gums, which the old would call "albulus"; it is necessary to hold this with forceps, cut it at its root and allow blood or blood to flow out. Then place it under the vitriol burn, or other drying and desiccating powders; if that flesh returns after the incision and repeatedly appears, cut it again secondly and cauterize it: if it doesn't return even after being burnt with a cautery; these are the methods for cutting out this tissue.
des sordens	From the sounds
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Some times they are gathered at the top of the teeth roots, inside the mouth between the gums, those that are ugly and rough; and sometimes the tooth turns black and yellow and worms, until corruption reaches the gum, and the tooth becomes stinky; then it is necessary to make the patient sit with their hands on yours, and the head should be in your palm, and pull out any teeth or roughness as long as nothing remains; and so you deal with darkness and greenness, yellowness, and other tones, until they are all gone; if what comes off at the first attempt is correct, it's good; if not, start again from the second day and third onwards, until you have everything removed; and know that teeth require various types of instruments to be pulled, according to what their craft demonstrates, for the rasp used to remove teeth above them has other forms than those used in between them; and these forms and others should be with you prepared.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	When you treat a tooth for its pain, it is necessary that you wait as long as possible to pull the root out, because one should not do this too hastily; indeed, the process should be conducted slowly. This is due to the fact that if done too quickly, one might make an improper cut, and thus no excuse exists for hastily removing a tooth.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant. Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	So when the patient is forced to bleed, it must be certain about which tooth causes pain. Many times, with toothache, one should consider if it's a wisdom tooth causing issue, and pull out the good tooth; and throughout this process, do not let the pain disappear completely until the bad tooth has been removed; for we have already taught our surgeons to handle these procedures; and when you are certain about which tooth is causing trouble, it is necessary to scorch around the tooth with a strong spatula to keep the gum intact from all sides. Then move it into your hands or under delicate tweezers gently until they are well dislocated, then firmly secure the tweezers; have the shoulder of the patient in your holy grip between your knees, and hold it tightly so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier. Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	After the tooth is extracted correctly without breaking it off, and if it doesn't fall out on its own, take none of these tools and gently push it in from every part inside each section, then move it around like you did initially. And should the tooth be pierced or damaged, it's necessary to fill it with cloths where they're lost; and when extracting it delicately with tweezers, ensure that it doesn't break during extraction; and it must be very carefully opened around the gum in order to extract the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere. Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And make sure you do not break it and leave a part behind, causing more severe toothaches than before due to the pain of the root. Remember not to act like unaware surgeons who with their haste and boldness break everything down once, then don't follow our advice; but they cause this disease by repeatedly getting into the root or damaging the jawbone each time, as we often tell them. And when the tooth has been extracted, wash the mouth with wine or vinegar and salt; if bleeding starts (which is common), fill the mouth with vitriol powder. If that doesn't work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the tools, to which one binds their teeth first, should be with long points and thick handles, so they do not double when you pull the tooth; and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let them have large parts that do not bend while being pulled, and be made of well-crafted iron, and have teeth for holding things in place.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre .i. jor ou ij., tant que li leus soit amolis, puis i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	When the root remains during extraction, it is necessary to put in place a wet cotton swab saturated with oil for one or two days until the gums are softened. Then remove the forceps known as 'algefri', so that the shoulder appears to resemble a surgeon; and they should be made inside like a file, which is the shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these clamps, then it is necessary that you uncover the entire flesh right up to the root, and place the tool called 'althali', which is known as a palainche, as follows:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And let it be strong and thick so that it doesn't break at all, and if the root jumps over this, it's good; if not, use all your tools, as those mentioned next will come into play:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you assist with the tool having two points, as described here:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other tools located in front according to their place, and from this tool that seems like a pair of large tongs, as depicted here:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And be this one of your tools so that it may not break, and know that there are many types of dense tools; also other tools, which are not counted among the rest; and the wise masters themselves discover their own tool by themselves, according to what their work and disease reveal to them. For there are certain diseases where the old did not teach a tool because of the diversity in these ones, and if it breaks due to wear or from other bones, or if it decays, when they seek out the tools that suit them, that I have told you about, and aid with gestures, as what follows is their form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be large and well held to hold the bone, so that it doesn't escape, but can be held and removed; and then restore him to the place with medicines suitable for this, and if there is decay in the bone, and it is small, if you use all this instrument.
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to its natural form, and its shape is ugly, especially even in virgins, you must know if this tooth was born after another tooth, and it isn't placed straight, and one can neither file nor saw it: so you should remove it; and if it's next to a tooth, take this instrument that has the following form, and resembles two small beaks, and it is made of hard iron.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the dentist holds the molar tooth gently and very firmly with their hands for its hardness of the tooth surface, and because you do not move the others, and if it is visible that one can shave it off, then he shaves it with half of a file in this way:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And also like the file used to make needles; and he files the tooth gently in his hands softly, so that it does not move until it grinds; then makes the flat part at the end using all kinds of raspers, and if its edge is too sharp and hurts the tongue, then you must file down the roughness until it is even, so as not to hurt the tongue or impair speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth rots
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les .ij. dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a .i. ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper. Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des .ij. dens sains, et des .ij. meus, si com tu vois:	When the tooth in front of a hole appears through percussion or fall, and if it doesn't press upon what it's chewing that it doesn't defecate, and you've treated with medicinal restraints, and this isn't effective; then they must be restrained with an gold thread, for silver threads turn green and rot, but gold never changes. And the thread size should neither be too small nor too large, according to the space between the teeth; and if you notice that teeth are aligning themselves, take hold of the thread and braid it in between two healthy teeth, then place the dislodged teeth between your own teeth if there is one or more, until you see clearly up to the other side of a healthy tooth; then resume covering up to where you had covered before, and pull your hand gently yet firmly, so long as they don't move; and tie around the root of the tooth so that it can't escape. Then clip the threads with tweezers, assemble them, and place between the healthy teeth, making sure not to irritate the tongue; then leave it compressed in this manner for as long as it can stay without loosening or breaking, and if it does loosen or the threads break, you pull again with another thread; so it will remain compressed and serve its entire duration like this, and this is the form of teeth and the connection between two healthy teeth and two own teeth, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth aches, you put it back in its place, step by step, as we have said; and don't interfere with anything that isn't appropriate or tolerable, and never form the shape of an ox's bone tooth, and put it in the place where there is a defect, and hold it just like we've said, and remains and serves for so long.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	covering the tongue wound
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder. Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	No instance comes from within the tongue or nature that one is born with; or by chance due to healed wounds. The surgical procedures consist of working on the mouth near the ailment, have your head in proper alignment, and lift the tongue; then cut the nerve cord wide enough until the tongue has been dislodged from its position, and if there's stiffness or swelling, it might be a result from healing wounds, so pinch the hook and cut the affected part of that connection; and ensure the incision isn't made too deep for fear of an artery beneath; once finished, place the head in water of rose color and coolness, then under the tongue lay a linen cloth; and every night cleanse the patient, making sure no more bleeding occurs. And should there be bleeding again, pour vinegar into the head wound; if it doesn't stop, cauterize using the slow flame cautery which is suitable for this purpose; after that proceed with other healing methods until they've healed fully.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see that the ailment has turned to red or black or hard so that the patient doesn't feel it, do not touch it because it's gangrene; and should it turn from yellow to green and there be moisture, then pinch the hook and drain a thin pus, and cleanse from both sides; and if the wound discharges when you don't apply anything, pour vinegar on top until it is cleaned out, then return to your work until all strength has been applied; after that place the head in cool water and steam, and proceed with other treatments until they have healed fully.
des apostemes de la gorge	From throat abscesses
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les .ij. amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer. Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez. Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	No time comes within the throat bokes which are called 'godath', and they are properly termed as the two almonds. And when you treat them, just like we have mentioned in the division, if they're not healed, do be careful: should there be hard pus pockets of small sensation and be colored yellow or white, don't touch them with iron at all. And if they're red-colored and the root is large, don't touch them with iron either for fear of blood spilling; but let them remain until they bleed naturally, then you can remove them, or they'd rupture on their own; and should they be whitely colored, have a fine instrument ready to scoop out. But first check if the pus pockets are calmed down and in peace. Then place the patient under sunlight, ensure their arms are in good health, let them open their mouth and press their tongue between their hands of the servants, applying pressure with all the tools; this is how it's done; and have it made of silver or very fine brass just like knives:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Can't you press the tongue with all this tool, and see if there's pus? Take the onion and the point of the almond, pull it up more than you can; and don't remove anything from the threads with it. Then scoop it out with the tool; this is how it looks like a force; and every spot that was affected, one place then another, they're very sharp, and made of iron or brass:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you don't have this tool now, take the scissors; this is how it looks like:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And make an incision on one side and the other; and when you have completed one of the almonds, complete the other in the same manner, and after the incision, gargle the patient with hot, cold water, or cold and gentle water. If bleeding occurs during this process, then continue to gargle with hot water, or use cooked currant fruits, or rosemary leaves, or similar substances until the wound is healed; then complete the cure when it is healthy; and if any other abscesses form in the throat besides the two almonds, you should remove them accordingly like the two almonds equally.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir .i. aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi .i. jor ou .ij. Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis .ij. rains par les .ij. pertuis dou neis. Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un .i. oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	And I treated a woman of an abscess that she had inside her throat, to be precise, one small abscess. And almost the entire throat was blocked because it had been completely clogged, so the woman could neither breathe nor eat or drink and died within one day or two days since she couldn't endure this state. The abscess had grown quite a lot, and it had caused four ribs to be pushed up from her neck. I quickly acted, put an ounce in one place, then took out the thread, and removed a large portion of flesh with it; after that, I made another cut at the other nostril and got the mouth open, pressing on the tongue; afterwards, placed the thread into these abscesses, and took out some part from each, and only a little bit of blood came out. And thus opened the passage in her throat; she started to drink water now and then wine, and I didn't stop cutting this abscess for a long time; the abscess grew back immediately and filled up all that I had emptied, until it became quite large; after that, I treated her with cautery inside the throat: she didn't grow again. And from these parts, may God do as he pleases afterwards.
de l’uve	Regarding the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve». Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li. Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide. Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a .i. des .ij. estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres. Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor. Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague. Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	When the swelling comes down in the eye and it swells again, lasting long, it is named "perpendicular"; if it is large and round, it is named "eye". When it heals as we have said in its division, and treatment does not help, and you see that the wound from the abscess has calmed, and it becomes soft, then you should handle it; and one that is round assembled and not long; and it is bloody or of reddish color or black, then you must avoid making an incision on it. For there is great danger for the patient. So when you see it, according to the manner I have said, based on its size and length, make the patient face towards the sun, press their tongue with the instrument we mentioned earlier; then insert the needle into the eye, pull it outwards, and cut off one-half to three-quarters of what we have said in cutting the two almonds. And you should not remove more than necessary which is beyond the natural boundary; for if you remove too much, it causes pain and difficulty in speaking; after making the incision, use what we said about cutting the two almonds, then treat until it has healed. If the patient fears during the cutting process, you should apply a tool for cautery sensitive to their fear. And the method of cautery is sharp and precise. And make sure that the eye puts its head towards your healing area, then press their tongue with the instrument mentioned in the chapter about cautery, applying it with living force, so that it is neither too thick nor too thin; and use the movement of this tool as described here:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And put our head with some hair on which we apply the medicine, just like the movements of a spoon, and place the tool over all the medicine on the eye; and let the patient lie on their side so that saliva and mucus go from their mouth inside to the medicine, ensuring it doesn't descend into the throat or the stomach; then hold your hand with the medicine and press onto the eye for half an hour's quantity until you see its numbness and the medicine's impacts have calmed; if you notice, take cotton and wrap it in any tool, soak it with medicine, insert that tool inside the cotton all the way to the string, until the cotton dries on the eye; repeat this often, until the cautery is perfect, then let it dry, and close afterwards for 4 days or 5. If you need to restart the medicine's cautery, do so, and after the cautery cleanse around the eye with gauze soaked in butter, clean up what is inside of the medicine; rinse from cold water, and wash with gargling until it heals fully.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision, or with the cautery; if it is treated by fumigation in this manner, take camomile and hyssop and rosemary and rue and calendula and parsley and similar herbs, and gather all of them or some of them into one pot, then place it there, and bring to a boil; and ensure that the pot is well filled with strong earth, and within the pot there be two sticks as this method dictates:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut. Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And it can be made of silver or iron, and if you have two shoulder blades place them in the mouth near the illness until the vapor rises to the ovule through the nose, until the ovule is necrotic; after this begin often again, until the ovule dries up, and ensure that you do not perform this at the beginning of the appearance of pus-filled abscesses, for many things happen then; and do not use this method when the pus-filled abscesses are declining. And if this instrument is unavailable, take a reed and place inside your head an eggshell, so that the mouth near the illness is not too hot; for the eggshell does not cause the vapor to burden the mouth, and this collection of remedies will serve as a cure together in health.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times there is air in the throat bone or spine of fish, without any issue; therefore, it's necessary that you remove what you can see, and press the tongue at noon to all the tool, so that you can see if something moves; and if this doesn't reveal anything and remains in the throat, it's fitting that you make the patient vomit until the illness is expelled; by chance if the illness is pushed out through vomiting. Or if the illness swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a root of lettuce, or one chunk of dry bread; and tie the sponge with a thread, and then swallow it again; and when she comes to the head, if she is expelled by air, and then pull out forcefully; and if this doesn't work as described, take one tool of a plonc according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And prepare the instruments so that they may enter more easily into the throat, and have the head raised in the air; be careful not to touch the epiglottis, that nothing gets inside it or push bone inward; guide them well as the patient pushes out the instrument, because they will push if they move or if the thing is pressed; if it's pushed down by mouth, or it pulls forcefully on all of the instrument equally until she can pull it.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the lumen of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit. Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout .i. petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu. Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine .i. fer chaut, et fai ce sovent. Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor. puis pren plein .i. voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	No treatment is given for the throat fluid, as I have explained in the division, through medicine therapy; and when this doesn't help, then look at the patient's throat with the sunlight, then press their tongue against the instrument I've told you about. And if you see the throat fluid, then guide it out by half an uncia or with fine tongs suitable for this task. If that doesn't work, take a hair and insert it into the patient's throat where there is pain, then push or pull the hair with the effort of one hot iron several times, and repeat this often. And if the patient's throat becomes discolored by water all day long, then take a full glass of cold water, work their mouth with it, pour it inside without making them swallow, and move it around in their hand often; and as soon as the throat fluid smells the water, they will vomit.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier. Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes .i. pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And if she does not give birth as we have said, then fumigate the patient with asafetida, using the tool I mentioned for fumigation of the eye. Do this many times because it will relieve without causing pain. And concerning the method of fumigation, you take one pot containing charcoal sticks and cover its bottom with a small pierced covering in the center, then place the tip of the tool in this hole. Then pour your fumigation, put the end of the stick inside the mouth of the patient, seal their mouth so that no fumes escape but only go into the throat; and now the saliva will come out. If it does not come out, start the fumigation again many times. And let the patient suffer thirst, eat salty things, among others, and do not drink water; then it is necessary for her to relieve herself through this process.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the tool used to expel saliva is such that when it can be seen, it resembles curved scissors meant to enter the throat; and has the appearance of a doctor's snout, and it has a grinding quality like a rasp, so whatever she takes, she cannot leave it; and here is the form:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en .ij. manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor. Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors. car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	No mention of discharges is according to what memory comes after from one and another in this book, and they differ in perforation and size; it's in two ways where one is by its appearance itself, and due to the moisture that he has. And the second way it is by the bones in their position within the body. for discharges from the head are different from those at the foundation, and the discharges from the soft parts of the head are different from those which come into joints, and each has its judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures. Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre. Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	And if in discharges one must not pierce them until the body is dead according to its completion; and if there are such that it should be pierced when they have grown and do not die according to their completion, as discharges coming out of joints. For when discharges come out of joints, and you leave them while they are still within, by chance perhaps they corrupt the ligament and nerve in the joint, which is a cause of contraction in that limb. Or if the discharge is within the main body part, and if you delay perforation until it has been dead, it will harm the main body; or if it is within the foundation, piercing should be done once it has been dead; and it should not pierce a growing discharge without full digestion completion, except for that which is within the foundation, it could have broken through fully and remained inside, causing a tunnel to form; and cannot heal in great duration.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it must be that you know the time of the perforation of a discharge which is dead according to its completion, and this is when the pain has eased, and the departure of fever, and the diminution of pain and redness, and from agitation and sharpening of the head of the discharge, and other signs; and it must be that you place the perforation at or higher than the location of the discharge, and where it opens outwards; and have the perforation along the length of the body, and if the discharge is on hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and everywhere equal where there is no wrinkle.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre. Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit. Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui. Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.  Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com .i. drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en .iij. angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	In those that bend, according to the extent of the limb. And when abscesses are in the soft part of the body, you should only puncture them if they are confirmed by digestion completion process, as we have said. For if you pierce before this point, it will prolong within his body from the poison and be filled with much dirt; and accidentally harden his lips and deepen inside him. And for any abscesses that are pierced through the width of the body, according to what the limb needs.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites. Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois. Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those who do not have a head, such as superficial abscesses, it is necessary that you pierce them fully; and when the abscess is large, and has accumulated much pus, if you pierce it, you should not extract all the pus in that moment, but remove only part of it; then cover the abscess until the next day, then leave nothing else in it; do this repeatedly from large to large, until the pus completely escapes; even if the patient is weak or a woman bearing, children, old and decrepit. For each time there's an escape of pus with the exit of the pus, the patient might die, and you would not know about it. Therefore, be careful in this chapter and when you have pierced your abscess, if the wound appears, look to see if the wound from the abscess is small; and if it's a full cut, use linen or old cotton; and for large abscesses, and there are many punctures within, it should be that you stuff each one with a tent so they lie against each other; and if you have stitched in the abscess some part of skin, and sewed it together internally, then you should fill it with old cotton or linen rags without moisture, and bind it until the third day; then heal and apply ointment until it heals properly.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille .i. drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.  Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there's blood leaking from your vein, you should cool it down and keep it mild. And apply a wet cloth once or twice. And if the blood leakage persists, then take control of the situation and treatment, along with the powders I have mentioned in this book, and if it's in winter conditions, and where the veins or abscesses are very sensitive, it should be that you place wet tents and cloths soaked in wine and oil; and if it's summer condition, and the veins are soft, then you should cover them with cloths soaked in cold water and oil, or in chilled wine and oil until the third day, as we have said; and then remove and clean the wound properly, following what should be done, until it heals.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this must be known universally in treatments of abscesses: now I have told you how one should proceed before treating abscesses, and here begins the chapter.
des soros	of the womb
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances. Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire. Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout .i. estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient. Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc. Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit. Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se li apostemes tient .i. nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés. Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	Or small abscesses come from the womb and are in cloths, as with a knucklebone of a calf, and many resemble this. There are some that have moisture like little animals; and others have such that they are hard and stony to the surgeon, and there is no doubt that it's an artery if it doesn't go against this. And the work of the operation consists in trying with all one's instruments what is called "an entromissor", which comes after this form, containing something. For if it contains moisture, then you do this through its length. And when the moisture has been drained out, then scorch without leaving anything behind that contains such moisture, for it returns immediately once nothing is left; then immerse cotton in Egyptian ointment oil, if present; should there be none, in water and vinegar, and apply to the wound, leaving until the next day; and this heals what remains of the night. And thus you renew the cotton as before, on the second day, and the third, until you know well that it doesn't remain through the night; then treat the wound with ointment according to what is suitable, until it's healed. And if the abscess contains one or two fat grains, you cut according to this form, longitudinally; and you squeeze out all your remedies from it, and scrape around everywhere, and put your entire cure of draining force on the cloth where it lies; and if the artery gives back against this, then do as I told you after. And similarly with stone-like abscesses, and with cutting and treating as I told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc. Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut .i. apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere. En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	And when dealing with pierces and moist areas, it is lighter because there's less blood involved. And if there are no moist conditions in these pierces or their vicinity, and of these two pierces I described for the elderly woman; and found that the pierce was just like a hard stone, rough and white, and couldn't be broken; and if any had been made into it, one would have done as well with it as with a stone. In other pierces arriving or their vicinity, it was observed that those coming from the children's heads and the roots of the ears, the opening should always remain for several days at least dependent on its position, so that the poison may exit; and treat them accordingly.
des scrophules	Regarding the treatment of scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre. Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes. Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit. en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les .ij. levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	Many times a boil occurs in the neck, and when they are opened, and during infections, and nowhere else or on body parts, and are hard, being bound together. And each scrofula is properly confined within its bone, just like a nut or a boil at the head, as we have said; and there are many appearances of these scrophules. Some contain moisture, and others are malign, not willing to submit to treatment. In that case, you see good disposition in the surgeon's hand, resembling the color of the bone, being silent from each part and not touching the glands under the neck or arteries or ducts, nor being deep; it should be cut from above, and scrape off every part, and extend the two lips at the angles, if necessary, as we have said about boils. Treat gently and gently, make sure you don't cut the nerve or the vein, nor create too much heat and do not penetrate too far ahead, ensuring that you only cut what you are supposed to.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir. Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde. Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if you cut the vein or artery, and it does not allow you to open, then apply vitriol paste or any powders that stop bleeding in the wound, and keep the wound restrained; and let it remain as long as the abscess subsides and the wound softens and begins to heal. And when the blood has stopped flowing, return to your work until its completion; only then should you seek guidance according to your duty if there are still small scabs remaining, remove and clean them. If in the root of the scab there is large bleeding, it would not be suitable for you to cut that scab from its root but tie it with a double thick thread instead, let it heal naturally; then apply an old cotton pad soaked in Egyptian ointment to the wound and proceed with treatment.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les .ij. levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule. si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit. Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cut the whole scab, it is necessary for you to join together the two edges of the wound and stitch them now. There should be no excess remaining because of the size of the scab. It is fitting that you attend to cutting off its root and draining it thoroughly; then sew it as we have said earlier. Those scabs that retain excess, pierce wherever it opens and drain it. Do this similarly as previously mentioned, with dressing and other similar actions, so that they are corrupted where they remain from the corruption process; and when the wound is well cleaned, treat it with ointment until it heals properly; let it be covered by ointment and dressings while it remains healthy.
de squinance	The text "de squinance" refers to issues related to or conditions caused by malalignment or misplacement, which is a common theme in medieval medical texts dealing with anatomy and orthopedics. It could refer to deformities, dislocations, or other types of misalignments that affect parts of the body such as joints or bones.
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The old ones spoke of the surgery to alter the throat; but I never saw anyone do it in our land, and that is written from their speech.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those who have squinting vision, it is necessary that the incision of the throat called 'epiglottis' be avoided; and one should not take help from this, because all the veins and the heart are at risk for those who have a foreign body in their mouth, or in the throat or between two gums.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is within the channel of the heart, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid the loss that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz .iij. cercles ou .iiij. une petite fendure dou travers, entre les .ij. cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	Therefore, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, it is necessary to make three or four small cuts across, between the two circles, by the amount of the cut through the skin but not into the cartilage;
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	And those bones are suitable for cutting the epiglottis where there is no flesh, and the vessels are long from there.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	And if the surgeons are fearful, it is necessary that they extend the skin of the throat to all parts of the neck, then cut through the skull until it reaches the chin; and avoid blood vessels, should you see anything, and then perform the operation as we have described.
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	And it is demonstrated by the section of the vein in the chin that blood jumps through the side where the bone is broken, and due to the loss of voice.
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And leave the wound open for a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the time has passed since one doubts strangulation, gather the two edges of the wound neatly, and all along the skin until the cartilage; then administer medicines that cause flesh to grow, as long as it is healthy.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim asserts that one should not perform this until the throat is entirely swollen, and the patient's organs are judged dead, and the defect has been made.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	So one should cut through the epiglottis because the organs cannot evacuate, and they breathe through the wound, and in this way, one is protected from death.
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en .iij. jors ou en .iiij.	And because of this, the old men commanded to leave the wound open until the illness's malady passes, and it has passed in three days or four.
Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	And then they commanded to stitch up the wound and treat it until it had been treated.
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist .i. coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw that a young lady took one knife, and stabbed it into her throat, cutting part of the windpipe.
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was called to treat her, and found her just as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound and found the blood that was issuing from it, and I saw well that there had been no opened vein or outlet but rather the windpipe, and the veins flowed through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hurriedly treated it, and once it was healed, I cleansed the wound as much as possible;
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and after she spoke again her voice was hoarse, then she returned to being in good health.
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I swear by heaven that there must have been no defect in the tailoring of the epiglottis.
de la grosse gorge	From the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	Cysts of abscesses are called 'throat hernia', and they are large abscesses in the color of a chestnut, and are very common in women;
et est selonc .ij. manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	and there are two ways: natural and accidental; or natural has no belly.
Et li accidens est selonc .ij. manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accidents are according to two ways, one of which resembles a mass within us, and the other way resembles an abscess that comes from our artery;
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	And there is fear, it does not allow for large cuts only in those who are small, and the proof and search takes place throughout the entire surgical intervention:
se tu le trueves ausi com .i. nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	if you find it as well as a small rodent, and cannot pierce any vein, if you operate, as one operates on a mouse, and work out its entire body, if there's anything;
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	and search well inside, and treat it according to what is appropriate, until it is completely healed.
des nous	from the mouse
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	Many ways are there for us, so I will describe all the possibilities;
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	and it is fitting that I should explain all the differences between us and dislocation.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that dislocation is marked by heat and fever until the boiling has passed and decay been completed; thus the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient .i. syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With dislocation, there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and contains one gallbladder, which is its own sac and is according to the color of the body, and begins also like a boil, and becomes large.
et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	And according to two appearances, or greasy, or moist, and none of colors as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the treatment of a new wound, that you first test and inquire about every tool which is called 'entrainer', according to its shape or chapter that comes after.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the method for inquiring about pus in wounds is that you take or more moist substance than what you find in the pus, and make your fingers move little by little, until you know that the tools have reached the core, then according to the size of the pus;
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	Then remove the entrainer, and be careful not to jump while doing so.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	When there is moisture, it cuts through whatever material it has, if it creates an opening like I have described for other abscesses;
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	And if after the incision there is no moisture, know that it has been fat, then cut it across instead, and take hold of it with tweezers, gently scrape it from both sides, protect the area where it was located by covering it, and pull out the limb in good condition with a stick;
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	And if you cannot remove it cleanly, then remove it piece by piece so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if nothing remains, it will return to the wound repeatedly;
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if it stays for a bit, and the lack doesn't bother you, use certain corrosive water powders on the wound, hold the wound steady, place things that relieve in an abscess warm, and treat other treatments until it heals.
et se li nous est grans, si cout les .ij. levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	And if the lack is large, tie the two sides of the wound together, and treat the one who has ingested flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the vein is too large or goes against the grain and rushes you, tie off the wound, and use the lead of vitriol in small portions, and let it sit for two days or three, as long as the wound heals from within, then rest with a bloodletting; afterwards return to your usual treatment.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de .iij. manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a .iij. quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et .i. qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de .iij. manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	Here are the forms of surgical instruments used for insertion, and there are three ways: large, medium, and small; and among them, there are four squares called 'albaret', and one called 'breb', and among these, there are three sizes: large, medium, and small, to encircle the abscesses.
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	And they are also like the needles from which one removes the thorns, and they are made of amber citrine, or iron, or silver, and yellow ones are valued more than black beeswax because they excel in surrounding the curves of fistulae;
et sont de .iij. manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	And there are three ways: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the width of the defects.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures de .iij. manieres ausi;	The shapes of the pins resemble sheep, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and if there are two curves in the pins also in three ways.
et si a oncines qui ont .iij. corbeures, et sont ausi de .iij. manieres; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de .iij. manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	And if there are pins with two curves, they also come in two ways; and if there are pins with two curves and single-curved pins, and these all come in two ways; and all of this is necessary in their location.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The head of this one that they make to be sharp, and among such ones who cut not force but from one side, which they sear the skin. For in this manner there is neither cutting of the vein nor nerve;
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	And these introducers have their pincers in hand so that the patient does not feel them during the opening of abscesses;
et sont de .iij. manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	And there are three ways: large, small, and medium, as you see;
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	and one uses no force but in the leg muscles, such as legs and arms, and nipples, and at joints, and similarly to them;
et aucune fois fait on .i. autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	And no other small instrument is used at all, resembling the pieces of pestles, according to this shape, to which one stops the blood flow:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	And it is placed only once at its natural location in the body, near veins and arteries, and never according to this large shape:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	The breasts of some men do not swell when they begin to become corrupted, until they look like breasts of women;
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne b. jusques a .g.:	And remain ugly and swollen, and if someone wishes to treat them, they should proceed according to this method described in line B up until point .g:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then scrape off the fat, and apply medicine to the wound that stimulates healing flesh. Then join together both sides of the wound for stitching. And treat it until it is healed.
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en .ij. costelz desus, par .ij. semblans fendures;	And if the belly rolls down and is flattened due to its size like it happens in women, when they divide it into two above, by two similar cuts;
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	From which one holds to the other at the end of one and the other, so that the longer line contains the shorter according to this form, from this line B up to the line G;
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les .ij. levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then scrape off the skin that is between the two edges, and remove the fat, and apply what we have said about stitching and powders, and what is necessary for treatment, until it heals.
