et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant,	And then I restarted, and exposed the bone as before,
et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	And I found the continuous corruption within the bone, and the arrowhead, and then extracted the bone, and bent towards soldering the socket;
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole,	but I could not manage it until I cut out about half of the bone, and then I pulled it with all its strength;
puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment,	then I returned him to medicine treatments; and he quickly recovered and was joined together;
et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir,	And can no longer begin the operation again except due to the weakness of the disease, which cannot endure,
et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and for fear of death that I have for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement,	For by the blood evacuation often occurred, but it was fully healed,
et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	And in the place of the bone there developed a hard flesh, and it was well arranged and did not cause harm or opposition at all to everything, neither from inside nor outside.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if any bone is broken within the body, then it should be treated in this manner:
pren .i. liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert,	Take hold of it and firmly grasp the end of the bone that has come out,
et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	and command him to extend it upwards;
et met .i. autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os,	and put another tie of thicker linen than the first one, and fasten it over the flesh that is around the bone,
et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz,	And remove the head if you bring the putrid flesh away,
et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and uncover the meat at the place where you see sinew, that the sinew not harm the meat;
et met .i. tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and place one ember or a board under the bone to make a barrier against the putrid flesh;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and you should do this as much as you can see and feel the corruption, and again do it another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie,	And if the bone is spoiled and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part,
si descuevre la char toute; puis met .i. tison desoz,	if you uncover all the flesh; then place one ember over it.
et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption .i. poc, si com nos avons dit;	and then apply the embers from one part to another of the corruption, and let the application cover for as long as the length of the corruption is two inches, just like we said;
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is at the joint, then cut out the corrupted joint, and apply heat to the bone on the other side;
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des .ij. jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	And if corruption exists at the point where two joints continue together, if there's no other artery that overlaps this location;
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose,	And if corruption is found in the part of the hand or around the foot, such a thing occurs quite forcefully,
mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	However, it still needs to be ascertained how this corrosion opens;
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and cleanse it in all the ways you can, but without opposing the vein or nerve.
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous,	And know that there are many knives and saws for cutting these bones, according to the shape of the bones and their appearance,
et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and their size and their delicacy, their grandness and their smallness, their hardness and their softness;
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and thus it must be equipped with each form of its instrument for its work.
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art,	And know that the task will show you the tool you need, according to understanding of this art,
et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	And the testimony of the manners of diseases;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	so choose the instrument you need according to what is suitable.
dou feu	with fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The shoulder dislocates either internally or due to heat;
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	And when you have cured that corrosion through the use of medicines, and if they do not benefit,
si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient,	then it is necessary to cover that limb up to its joint where the corrosion occurs,
si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	so that the patient does not escape from death or through cunning which is greater than the fault of the limb;
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu,	and it's a sign when the limb becomes black, as if it had been burned by fire.
et porrist aprés la noiror, puis va celle corrosions de membre em membre,	And after the darkness, then come those corrosion of limb by limb,
et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper,	And take over the whole body; if you hurry with copper,
et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans,	And if it's through the impact of some venomous beasts, such as sea scorpions and snakes, and similar ones,
se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	And if it affects the head from the neck downwards, if you treat it, and do not give it room to reach up to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it reaches up to the hand, if the cut is made at the joint, so that the wound does not extend up to the elbow;
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors,	And if it reaches the arm, if the incision is made at the arm; and if it goes beyond the cut, then many die.
et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	And its value is not to exceed that which its virtue allows;
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	And do it in the same way whenever a cut comes or piece: if it comes at the first joint, then after the second joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	And if she comes to a bone or joint, then cut all of it;
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	And if she ascends towards the leg, then cut at the knee joint;
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	And if it comes above the knee, there is no other option but to let the patient die.
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz,	And the method of tying or securing a limb is that you tie it above and below,
et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont,	Stretch one surgeon's hands on the lower ligament, and another surgeon's hands on the upper ligament.
et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les .ij. liiens a .i. spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	And you cut through the flesh that is between the two ligaments to an extent of one spatium wide, until the bone is exposed;
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part .i. drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain,	Then you cut through the skin and place one piece of linen on each side, ensuring that the healthy part is not touched;
et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And instruct another surgeon to inspect any other wound or abscess.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment,	And if blood spillage occurs when you operate, quickly cauterize the wound.
ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie,	or you put some constricting powders; then return to your medicine until its completion,
puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then bind the unaligned member with a reliable bandage, and treat it until it heals;
et je te conterai k’il avint a .i. home en som piet:	and I will tell you what happened to someone once in such a situation:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu,	He experienced a blackness that seemed like fire.
et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	And this corrosion came first to his knee joint, until it consumed the entire leg.
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	And when the honorable saw the corrosion, he sought to cover his leg, and became healthy;
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi,	And for many years after that, the corrosion came to his hand again, and it reached me.
et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	And I placed him on things reactive after the purification of the body, and could not stop the corrosion.
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	And it was that I would pass my hand over him, but I would not, for I had hope of reflecting the matter.
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist,	I also doubted whether if I cut off his hand, he wouldn't die from it.
car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre,	For the strength of the ome was weak; and he completely lost hope, and returned to his land.
et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	And if they are able to cover their hand, and if they have sanity;
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I have only included this for the sake of doing something else, if necessary.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	No abscess ever comes in a person's inner flesh, and stays for so long that it causes an assembly of worms;
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	And then they grow and penetrate, and the worms jump, and remain in a person's veins, just like vessels;
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez,	And the skin above is also as delicate as one tunic of fine material,
et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain»,	and do not extend up to the bone or nerve, and such diseases are called 'sane' in this way,
et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and is not called 'fistula';
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it extends so far as to reach the bone from within, then it is called 'fistula';
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	And the cooking process is such that you must thoroughly cook this skin all around, and likewise when it's delicate, just like a piece of fabric;
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and doesn't rot due to its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont,	And if you have chosen that the skin dries out, and the corruption isn't at perfection,
et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	and if the skin is thick with flesh, then cleanse it like this:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor,	Look to see if his breasts are large, and the nipple which is on him has a stinking smell,
adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	Then administer an Egyptian enema made as follows:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en .i. vassel au feu,	Take aloe, and oil, and litharge, equally, and cook them together in one liter pot over the fire,
tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	Continue cooking until the medicine turns red, and thickens to the consistency of honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel,	And then take from this according to your need, and do it with water and honey,

de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the incision of the nail

la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain originated from the hand

Des vils	Of cauterys of fire, commandeth to the malaise to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they pricked at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.

De la voinne civile	From the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is placed in legs, in warm areas where no herbs or trees are born, and in soil that has no moisture;

Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Worms that are born between the skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This disease is called in our land "cow disease", because it happens many times to cows,
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	and it is a small worm that is born between the skin and muscle, and travels throughout the body going up and down,
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	and one feels it moving from member to member, as far as the skin where it was going, and jumps out;
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and is filled with corruption of some fluids, like worms and roundworms or in the stomach;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	And there's doubt about its nature, for when it travels through the body, and ascends to the head, and comes to the eye,
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	by chance enters, and destroys the eye; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it being treated and healed, one cannot but observe when it is going:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	So it follows that you should bind the wound above and below with a strong, tight bandage,

et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming near to the eye or head, then restrain over him the eyelid, lift it up and pull on it gently;
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	And it is necessary to use the means of purification of bodily fluids from medicines, to combat the impure humours.
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	And it is warned about eating spoiling meats that cause putrefaction.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of the pain that comes from wind disturbance
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This illness is called in our land "vakiiri", and it is a pain that comes to some limbs,
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	And thus from member to member; and I saw what I told you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was summoned to care for an afflicted woman, and she showed me her arms, revealing a small swelling in the vein of one arm;
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	And just .i. inches later, I saw it rise as high as a worm on its shoulder,
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	quicker than nothing at all, like quicksilver when it's cut from one place to another;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	The pain departs from that side, and pierces into the shoulder,
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	And then a little later spreads throughout the body, until it reached the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	Then I noticed that it was twisting inside the body, just as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled much at how she moved from member to member in this manner, for I had never seen this disease like this before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	In any case, I have wanted many that well had wanted to move pain of him to another,
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I did not want it as much, as I see in the woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	and I thought it was because of that which caused the woman to have a wet body and her veins exposed,
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and from this, this weakness becomes apparent;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	And they do not appear according to this reason among those who are delicate, and have moist bodies and responsive veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you see the treatment of this illness, and if the patient feels pain, if it opens like we have said,
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	if it rises quickly from above and below, then apply pressure until that wind's force is released out of the body;
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	and cauterize the area; and if you do not see it at your eyes,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	If you are treating someone whose veins have been disturbed, as with stinking pills, pills made of snake venom, and similar others.
Des saiettes	Of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are various, depending on their shape and where they pierce the body.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The variety of their sizes means that there are those with large points, and small ones, and barbed, and soldered;
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	And of those with two angles, and those with tongues, and of those where there are fragments;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	And the one who urinates in no member but does so according to two ways: or in the main body it urinates,
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	just as in the brain, heart, liver, kidneys, lungs, intestines, bladder, and similar organs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	And when it urinates then in no part of these organs, the signs of death, which I will tell you later, become evident to you:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	If you need to perform the extraction of this arrow, because death comes later in multiple situations;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	And if you don't notice the bad sign and the arrow isn't fully out, then pull it and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And when the sign of the brain occurs when the arrow hits and pierces the bone, and the wind springs up that is above the brain.
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	It's when blindness and numbness occur along with swelling in the eyes, and redness of the tongue, inflammation and redness of the mouth, and muscle spasm and confusion of mind, and vomiting of bile;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	And perhaps it is without strength in the nostrils, or in the ears; and by chance it loses speech and voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	And from the wound comes white moisture resembling pus, and also in the leap as burnt flesh does;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And if this sign appears to you, take control of the treatment, and pull out the arrow if it hasn't become embedded.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the arrow when it strikes or pierces is that it's near the left breast, and also if it seems to be embedded in something hard rather than empty.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	And by chance the patient might lose sensation as well as the hair, with black blood bleeding out, and coldness and cold sweat, and fainting:
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	Therefore, you must be aware that many die in doubt.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow that never comes out is when there's no foam escaping from the wound, and the throat swells up, and the patient has a changed complexion, and breathes loudly and feels cold.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow exits through the armpit area, it is located beneath the ribs; and there's copious bleeding and intense pain, with labored breathing; and all limbs move freely from the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if an arrow or stomach is stuck, by chance something from the undigested meat comes out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if an arrow or stomach is stuck in the chest or abdomen, and nothing comes out through the intestines, there's no hope for treatment, nor in extracting the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if an arrow or stomach penetrates into the bladder, and urine comes out in spurts and exits, causing great pain to the patient: you should know that this wound is fatal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other parts of the body, such as the limbs (including arms and legs), neck, throat, shoulder blades, shoulders, shoulder girdle, back spine, ribs, and buttocks, along with any similar limb, are safe according to various dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When an arrow is in the muscle or artery, and it isn't poisonous, as I will tell you what happened to me, because you did this other thing.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened at the first house when an arrow struck him in the middle of his face below the nose:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried it, and I pulled it out from the other side through the fat behind the ear; there was no severe damage.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And removed an arrow that had fallen in the fat by the eye, under the eyelid,
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	And the arrow had been removed, yet one could not reach even its tip towards the shaft,
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And the arrow was as long as an Oriental bow, not even one inch heavy without any ears; the wound was cleansed, and no unfortunate events befell it.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And drew out an arrow from the throat to a Christian, and the arrow was Arabian with ears:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I pulled at the barbs, I was skillful as I drew it out, and the Christian was cleansed.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And try to extract an arrow from his right side, where he was pierced or in his belly, and I thought that he was dying;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then since it had passed thirty days, if it did not change its position;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut near the arrow, and I tried to remove it with force, and there was no bad incident.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you see an arrow has fallen or been struck on one of your two sides, and the wound is healed up to;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	The arrow stays within, not reverting to its natural positions.
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	There is no harm found in any of its natural works.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And to another man, who was hit by an arrow on his face, and the wound was sealed;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And thus it did not allow him to endure great pain; and many others were like this.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And there was an arrow shot from one and a half yards away at the king's princes' home, where it was stuck in the middle of their nose,
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and was slightly leaning to the right side; and the arrow was completely inserted.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was summoned for treatment after it had been stuck in for three days. I found the wound extremely tight.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I tried to remove it with all my skill, yet failed to feel any movement;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	And he felt a wound and pain spreading over his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow.
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I placed a healing and digesting plaster on his head because the ears were not inflamed;
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	And I saw that the tip of the arrow was in the ear.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I placed the plaster on for days, and resolved the wound quickly, and thereby kept the patient under treatment for a long time.
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	Until he felt the arrow within his nose; and I told him about it.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I applied corrosive medicine to the wound for several days until it was opened up.
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	and I probed it, and felt the tip of the arrow moving towards the top.
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	Then adjust during the opening of the wound through this medicinal application, until the head of the arrow becomes visibly apparent;
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and make sure to pass well the ends inward for four months,
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	then loosen so that I could grip the edge of the wound, and press with both hands on either side, and it couldn't come out;
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	so I continued to refine and engineer ways for instruments until I took it on the second day using well-made pincers,
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	According to how its shape will come at the end of this chapter, as long as I'm treating it, and will heal the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And they judge that the cartilage near the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I will then treat it, and缝合 the wound, and healed the patient completely.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	And I told you about the quality of extracting certain arrows,
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	if you place your treatment on what I do not say, for books cannot encompass everything;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but let the wise masters compare well to a small number of things, and to what is present and lacking.
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Discover nine works, and nine instruments, for the removal of foreign matters that occur in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that arrows do not stay in the limbs where they are stuck according to two ways:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	By the arm where they enter, or from another side;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	And when it jumps in through a wound or where it enters, that is the arrow entering the flesh, and it will now occur for no other time.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not jump in now, leave it until the wound is healed internally, and wait for its natural exit;
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	And likewise if it has been driven into the bone and cannot come out, leave it like that for several days, and remove it every day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And then she jumps, and if she does not jump, it penetrates through to the entire depth of one slender hole, as long as the lungs are wide inside, and then removes it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if an arrow is lodged in the bone of the head, and goes up to one of the cavities of the brain,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	and some of the events that I have mentioned appear to the patient: if he does not remove her but leaves her until she becomes even after a few days,
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	because if the arrow reaches up to the brain, that is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	And if the arrow is only fixed in the bone, not coming until to its depth,
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	Let the patient rest for several days without any mishap, if there is no bad turn in the situation.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply stuck like that and cannot come out, if you administer trepanation inside, as I have told you; then treat the head until it becomes healthy.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is returned inside the body so well that one cannot see it, then seek for it with all the means;
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	And if you can sense it, guide it with any suitable instrument;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	and if you cannot do so due to the tightness of the wound, and because of the depth of the arrow,
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and there is no bone, nerve, or vein, cut as much as to make the wound large;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	and remove the arrow if you can, and if it has ears that hold it in place,
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	If bone has become embedded at two parts within you, then remove it as far as you can.
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and then break or bend the arrow's ears (feathers), until you can drain them;
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And do this carefully so that you don't break the arrow, but draw it out more forcefully.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you can't do it in one go, let the shaft be broken up to where its fletching is, then try again, for the extraction should be done quickly.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if bleeding against you runs contrary, then apply what we have said about treatment within our chapter;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	and beware of incisions near nerves and veins, and use your skill to draw out the arrow without risk,
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	or quickly or carefully, firmly or gently; and guide the patient according to the shape they were in when the arrow struck them.
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	because it is of great help that he be guided like this, and if you cannot do so, follow the instructions shown to you by the sign.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from elsewhere, or if it exposes any part of him, or if the skin is swollen in such a way that one can see or feel it clearly:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	Then cut upwards, as long as the tongs can take hold, and then draw [the arrow]: if you can jump now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, turn your hand around as long as it enters the bone, and enlarge the bone, then pull it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if she cannot come out, let her still be there, and then try the extraction again until she comes out;
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	And if the tip of the arrow is there, it is pulled all along the shaft;
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	And if it's at the base, and you see an arrowhead being administered, if you administer with a needle instrument of one kind,.
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	so that the tip of the arrow enters into the hole of the tool; and then force it.
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if the arrow is stuck, I use another needle tool with an entering point to facilitate extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if an arrow has touched it, then you must cover all the flesh around where it entered, if you can.
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	Then treat the wound as it should be treated.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if an arrow hits the head or wounds any part of the body, including the bladder or ribs, and it's close to vital organs, you should cover it; if you can cover it, do so.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and protect yourself from covering the vein and nerves, then remove the arrow, then suture the wound if necessary.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And the treatment until she is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The form of the tongs used to remove arrows resemble an animal's beak, and here is the form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And they come in different sizes: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape of the feather part is also like the feathers of a bird,
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	in order to reach the tip of the arrow, as illustrated below:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of the pincers for clamping and extracting is as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of veins from common sources
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	The veins from which we bleed are thirty-one, of which there is an outlet for sixteen.
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	This is to know: two small things which are after the ears, which are called 'the two herbs';
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	and the two arteries which are in both temples visible;
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and the two veins that are in both eyelids of each eye, which are called 'aspirants';
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is embedded in the forehead; and the vein that is behind the nose on the head.
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two kneading hands that are on the chest;
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are above in the lips of the mouth, and they are the veins that are called "aughers";
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and the two veins that are on the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The veins through which we usually bleed are five in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	The first is the one called the cephalic, and it's situated on the left side of the head, and they call this 'the vein of the head';
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	And the middle one is called 'the fast,' and it consists of the cephalic and the basilic;
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	They call this 'the vein of the heart'; and the basilic is either on the right or left side.
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	They call this 'the vein of the belly'; it is located near the groin.
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	And this is for the cure of which one becomes aware, which becomes manifestly apparent through the pouch.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	And the salvation is the vein that's located between the index finger and the ring finger, and if it's at two inches;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	And in the leg and where the foot is, there are three veins: one of which is below the knee on the left side of the body,
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	And the second one is located above the ankle on the right side of the body; and there's a vein called "the nesse", which is in the ankle on the other side.
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	And on the other leg are two veins under those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The health of the veins that are behind the ears is aided by ancient catharsis and in migraines;

Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The treatment of a vein wound on the forehead is just as important as the treatment for ancient diseases of the face, and headaches, and fever;

Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The wound of the vein near the nose is treated with bleeding, and hot fomentation, and diseases of the face,

Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The health of the two kidneys aids in the tightening of the alaienne (a type of intestinal disease), and at the beginning of melerie (melania or melanosis), and for many diseases, and in impetigo, and in corrosion, and in herpes, and estimomenes;

De la sainie des leivres	Of the health of the liver

De la sainie desoz la lengue	From cleaning under the tongue

Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The veins in the arm that we commonly heal are treated according to two methods:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	If it is touched by any one flame of a large iron candlestick, or by an olive oil lamp that is finely made like a blade, and called "aneil";

et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	And sometimes swellings occur in some men, such as during the first time, but they cause no pain.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of health depends on your thoughts.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing you need to know about surgery is that surgery is managed for the purpose of preserving health,
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	and to avoid future diseases;

que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	so that the vein doesn't burn and rupture upon being pierced.

si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	if you're in hurry, place a wet sponge with some warm water and a pinch of salt on the head for an hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	And it is necessary that you do this after the blood issue from the vein, and if it stays in place for several days without any darkness or greenness, if it does not harm the person;
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if you see this, place some aloes or myrrh in a juice made from calamus, mint, or something similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times there was pus and appearance in the healing of the basilica: so place your hand there, and if you find the part soft under the pressure of the hand, then it is an unpleasant appearance.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, do not apply any of what we have said to it, for by chance on the artery; but make one poultice of it dry to harden the part, then treat with another treatment until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each person with blood according to the quantity of its virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	But if the patient's blood is dark, let it only flow until it becomes red. And if you see it thick, let it continue until it thins out. And if it's too thin, allow it to cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And for the one who is robust and strong, needing blood extraction, it's advisable to make the incision larger, and have the flames wide.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	And for the one who is weak, do the opposite; make the treatment suitable and frequent, and the physician should treat it by cutting across, not straight.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And this method of healing saves from bleeding and the constriction of nerve, and is useful whether the wound is long or wide.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc .iij. fois ou .iiij.	And for the one whose body needs healing, it is necessary to give them a drink made from the juice of quince apples; if they are hot, they should be treated with bleeding three or four times.
Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And if they have a cold constitution, they should be treated before the healing with moilliet bread in a syrup made from muzé fruit; or in an aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, ensuring the syrup has a pleasant scent.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil,	And if they faint during healing, after bleeding has subsided, it is necessary for them to inhale a broth of blood and an aromatic syrup.
et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And apply the other things that we have said in the section or chapter on syncope, for the evacuation of veins.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wishes to bleed his arm and heal again, should it be necessary, when he is weakened by much healing, let him heal little by little, according to the strength of his remedy continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And if one wishes to bleed their arm after the first healing and they have strong veins, let them heal seven hours after the first bleeding or after the seventh hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And if one wishes to be healed on another side, they should be healed on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	For there is much blood inside the body that has already heated up, and it causes fever; so one must drain a large quantity of it, and widen the constriction until it flows freely.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson,	Since you have fulfilled all conditions of health, and place your hand on their pulse when it is healthy, so that death does not come to them instead of recovery.
et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	This happens many times when the healers are careless;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	And it should not happen when you see a limb dislocated and blood is forced out the second time, and if the constriction is closed, press forcefully.
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	If he is cuffed, stretch his arm quickly, because this would be harmful;
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer,	but let him until he heals the second time; or you touch the tip of the flame there, until the limb that is frozen from cold comes out,
et met sus .i. poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	and place half an ounce of salt boiled in water and gently press it on lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, let it be alone and do not compress it, until the abscess calms down.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if the need is to bleed again from the second time, if it lies within its own place or in another vein, or on the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein is treated in its place within the arm because it's made up of that vein from the head, since she is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the method of treatment involves having the patient immerse their hand in hot water until the skin turns red;
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	Then it should be half bound, so that the vein appears clearly. Now treat him through, not wide nor long;
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	And if the wounds are wide, and if the veins are well close to the joint of the hand, and if one cannot let them out, then put your hand in warm water, and leave the blood to flow in the water, until you have enough.
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	And if it's ice-like, do not reset your hand in warm water, for you put it more into winter than into ice;
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And this vein's laceration is safer from all others, for there are neither artery nor nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The treatment of saving the right hand from all liver diseases is valued against all illnesses, and this is how:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	Strengthen your hand, and hold it in hot water, as long as the vein is visible, if you can see it;
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and if it's inflamed from side to side, and if you hold it completely around everywhere, so that nothing hurts;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char,	and don't overheat too much on the inside, for the nerve is all bare of flesh,
et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and then immerse the hand in hot water, if the wrist is frozen at the wound site, and it cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as much as your skill allows, place a hot iron on the wound and seal it for rapid healing, and thus proceed with each case.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The cure for someone in the left hand is akin to the sickness of the mouse [a tool or method], and do all as I have told you for the right side.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors,	The cure for the spleen is effective against all diseases that are within the body,
si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	such as diseases of the lungs, and congestion of flowers, and spleen disease, and leg and old foot ailments, and similar illnesses.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere,	And the quality of its health is such that the patient should immerse their finger in hot water, and rub it over the vein until it discharges.
et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	And above the joint of the foot; and the veins are at the ankle, and from above the heel they flow into many rivers.
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	Healthy therefore whichever larger river, or at the ankle, flows like that which moves.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you heal it above the heel, be aware of the nerves that are nearby, and heal through as well as when sewing; let the flames be after this.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if they cannot come out, you should place the part in water, and let it empty well from the vein.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And when they are able to be inserted for the first time, if you try a second time above slightly more, because the limbs are salty;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	Nor should you doubt about the nerve, as we have said, and do the same procedure on the other limb equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The leg of the sciatic vein is at the ankle on the right side, and its health matches the pain in the hip, when it's due to hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	And the quality of its health is such that the disease enters through bathing, and it is drawn up above the anklebone. Four times in twisting,
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	for otherwise it does not open the vein; and if it opens, heal it in all possible ways that you can, and across it;
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And be sure to hold onto her, for the liver is there, and she responds greatly to human hands.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you can't find it, if there's no opening or wound on its front or back and belly, and towards the small spine, and beware of the nerves;
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And make sure to drain the blood as you see fit, then release the knot, and place cotton there and tighten it; now it is healed.
Des sainies de ventouse	Cures with suction cups
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Suction cups are made of horns, or spiders, or snakes; and suction therapy can be performed in two ways: by bleeding and drawing blood, or without causing bleeding.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	And this suction which can cause injury is done in two ways: either immediately with fire, or without fire;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	and suction that is performed by causing injury and removal of blood is done in twelve ways across the body,
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	of which some are entirely within the head; and others are in the neck region;
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and two of them are on both sides of the neck; and one suction tool is under the chin;
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	And use the suction for both shoulders; and use suction on the boils;
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	And apply the suction cups to both arms; and apply suction cups to both legs;
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	And use the suction cup on both ankles; and suction does not remove blood, but rather small veins that are scattered in the flesh,
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	And by this it does not weaken me at all, as one does with bloodletting;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And it should not be administered, nor with any fire or without fire, in any disease that comes from overfullness, until all the body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if suction is necessary for a disease, or by habit, we should administer it each hour at the beginning of her period, or towards its end, and in between and at every moment;
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	because there are those who, when they need to suck, weigh heavily on the head;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and if for such people there is congestion and redness in their face, and on the head, and at the neck, and confusion in the eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	And those who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have lost their tongue, and cough up blood;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if there are such things that worry them, and they see through the nose blood and bones and other similar items.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we observe these signs, especially around the month mark, we instruct them to take blood suction after three hours on the third day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The treatment of the nose helps relieve headaches ... caused by the eyes, and it is not right for this to happen after the evacuation of all the body;
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	And this suction is used in the treatment of the scalp,
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	And it should not be used by those with a cold constitution, or who have fever, because this causes considerable harm to them;
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	And similarly, it is not suitable for those using the sweat bath, nor for those who suffer from cold diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And the one who frequently sweats off with it, becomes forgetful, and for this reason it is necessary to place the suction cup a little further down due to the risk of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	The ventilation of the thorax is located at the center of health and the basilica, and it is good for it to be narrowed below the belly.
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	and through the channel of the heart, and suddenly, and in replenishment;
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	And it is good not to press too much, for if she holds too tightly, there will be a lack of sensation or stomach and heart.
Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	Ventilation at two places under the collarbone is useful for chest pains, eye issues and toothaches, as well as in strangulation, and for pain in the roots of teeth,
et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	And it is in the location of the healing of the basilica; and you must instruct the surgeon to expose his hand upon placing, not to cut the artery, and not to anticipate blood flow.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The ventilation under the chin is related to mouth diseases and gum decay, as well as other similar illnesses that occur in the mouth; it is part of the healing processes of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The ventilation of the shoulders corresponds to diseases caused by heat and congestion.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	Ventilation of the arms is equivalent to three veins in the arm,
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	for it has bled from these large veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and instructs the surgeon not to cut too deeply, because the limbs are naked of flesh, and there lies skin over nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The suction cup placed on the buttocks is useful for bleeding disorders from the bottom, and for diseases nearby, it is necessary that the suction cup be large, and made of leather, for she needs to be treated well; and by chance, if it were thin, it would break; and I make large wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The suction cups on the legs are applied openly, as they bleed throughout the body, and are useful for old pains in the kidneys, bladder, and uterus, and help to relieve swellings; and are at the places of the two shins, and the two ankles, and moreover, they weaken the body after long use, and cause fatigue in various conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The method of using the suction cup is as follows: you should place it empty first, and apply a steady suction, then quickly insert it, move it evenly, and keep doing this until you see the area turn red and swell, and observe the reddening due to blood; then remove it, and replace the suction cups again, take care of how each part is placed because there are those who have tough flesh and clear pores: one should pierce once only, and make wide wounds that are somewhat deep; and suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the wound is large, it should be pricked twice: the first time to pierce through the thick blood vessel.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the wound is very deep, it should be pricked three times; and when we wish to draw out a little blood at a time, we should only prick once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	And if we wish to retain some blood, we often reapply it; and if the wound is deep, we pierce deeply through it, and the ends are such that the vessels are pierced sharply.
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	It is necessary for the one with thick and hard skin, who have contracted sores, that you grease their lips with suction cups where an appetizing and liberating elixir appears:
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it is in the state of purple oil or sweet almond oil, or pumpkin seed oil;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it is yellow, use mustard oil, or lily oil, or chamomile oil, or any similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluity is large and cold, take turpentine oil, or balm oil, or fennel oil, and similar substances.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile,	And if you wish to strengthen the flesh and large pores, there should be no need to apply any oil.
mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	but it is suitable to wash after the suction with pink water, or cold water, or water from a rose, or water from a cucumber, or water from a porcelain dish, or other similar substances.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And for those with some moisture, if it is relieved by rest, or water from a myrtle and sumac, and similar substances.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have large excesses rise from old wine, or water of sulfur, or decoction of fennel or chamomile, or others similar;
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou .ij.; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion,	and there is no proper use of suction cups before the bath or in the bath, but one hour after the bath; and do not sleep afterward during suction treatment.
et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and it should be noted when he needs to be suctioned and when he has been suctioned.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And watch over those who are being cured if they are hot-tempered, and they become too vigorous and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	If it requires cold things, such as apples, endive and lettuce, and similar items;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And rabbit soup, and meat of a castrated male, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And for those with cold complexions, they should drink honey syrup and a half of aromatic wine that is between old and new, and eat small servings of rabbit soup, rabbit meat, young birds, and baby pigeons.
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	And on the day they are able to suck air, they should drink more than they eat;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	And it is necessary to give no one three times or musk before venostation, or after, in order to strengthen the main members;
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And sharpen the knives, but it is not proper that the hot ones drink.

Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the suction cup applied by fire is as follows:

En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the suction cup therapy for pleurisy disease, during all stages of the illness that are acute, there is no use of a tube or a plug, and it is administered only when it is full of water, and placed solely on the limb.
et c’est li forme:	and this is its shape:

Ci comence li livre des brisures	This begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	These chapters are many times necessary in the art of medicine, and restoration of breaks and healing.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know this, dear fellow, that the leaves of this chapter, which have been overlooked by the ancient books, no one has ever seen or read;

And in this chapter, I have described what is contained here and summarized it at the end, clearly showing the forms of the instruments that are used, just as I did in those two chapters before these.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, it is necessary that we outline or introduce the contents of this book with its principles and chapters where the mind accepts understanding, staying true to reality. So that those who have experienced it may know and learn this noble art and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when fractures or dislocations or twists or sprains occur to any part of the body, it is necessary for you to quickly treat the patient from one side and then the other. If there's nothing holding up on either side, such as weakness in muscles, children, or the elderly;
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	If the place where you press is too tight, or too cold; and eat cold meats, meaning frozen cuts, and liver and kid meat, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and do not fill up with foods that can fill the veins of blood, until you have doubt about a pus lump becoming hot, or spreading of matter in the body part; if the patient begins to improve after their first period under my treatment.

And when broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary that you introduce meats into the diet that cause substantial bloating or have viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water, and radishes, and onions, and peas, and beef stomachs, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar items.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	And with this type of bloating, the healing occurs more quickly and the breakage improves.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	Know that broken bones in the old and the weak cannot be properly set or sutured according to their nature because of the dryness of the limbs. mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet .i. gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	But do not hesitate to reset the broken bone. Work on the protruding ends of the bone and join the limb together again while it's strong as it was before; and don't stop halfway with your task. And for this reason, you should nourish yourself with large meat portions, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	Know that fractures can occur in various ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the heel or leg, and in this chapter, I will tell you all ways of fracture.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is cracking that goes to war, and another when sharpening, as with the size of a feather for writing.

et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois. Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. Another method for applying plaster to restore fractures and dislocations: take 30 raisins, dainy apples, rue, and asafetida, along with gum Arabic and mastic, each in an amount of .x.3; myrrh and aloes in amounts of .v.3; vinegar at seven parts out of eight. Another method for plastering in case of twisting: take mugwort and wormwood, each 1.3 grams; myrrh and aloes, each 7.8 grams; castor oil 6 grams; boric acid from Armenia 10 grams, grind them well together, then mix with water or enough egg whites, and administer it.

Another method for plastering in the restoration of bone fracture and for removing pus.
