Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Another way of plastering more forcefully than the first when pus hardens during member restoration. Take valerian roots, flax seeds, balm, lavender, and mint, and violet and chamomile flowers, from each one a part; grind them, mix with salt water or sweet water, or with wine, depending on the warmth of the limb and its rest period.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	In his book, Ippocrates instructs that for restoring strength to a broken limb, one should apply a balm made of wax and oil, and nothing else more. He states it should be neither too soft nor too hard but in between the two.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems that Galen suggests applying something to the broken limb for restoration, things that are dry but slightly warm, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar substances, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to plaster for injury and pain: take mussels and omelets' feathers or bird feathers, and basil, and lime of equal size, grind them, make a paste from it, and apply it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors	And then loosen a little afterwards, and be careful not to let the patient feel any pain, nor have the bone of its place move; if not loosen it by hands at all.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	And if pain comes to the limb, or itching, inability to rest or swelling, hurry and loosen it, and apply the plaster now; and take a light cloth, and a wet sea sponge, dip them in water, and cool off the limb, until the itching stops, and the pain is soothed.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	Then let the limb rest for an hour, afterwards place it on dry wool, moistened in water or rose oil, and bind it with a cloth until you are sure of removing pus.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let the inflammation settle in the limb, and relieve the pain, then begin the healing process subtly, with a bit of plaster, and do not apply pressure as strongly as before; and work delicately until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that pus is yellow and red, pain, swelling are present, indicating an abscess throughout, then you need plaster and binding, start again as you did the first time equally.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vij.; et aucune fois le laisse .xx. jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	And if nothing of what we've said happens to the limb, or if you can't release it until after three days, four days, five days, seven days; and each time leave it for twenty days, according to how things unfold, as long as the inflammation subsides, approaching the adjustment of the flesh.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	Therefore maintain the restriction longer than initially, and increase his meat supply, as I have mentioned before; and if you see that the body is drying out more than necessary, know that no improvement will come.
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	So regularly apply warm water to it whenever you reset the dislocation, and do this every third day, and relieve some tension in the joint.
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	Through this procedure then cut the dislocated parts of the limb and quickly counteract what the inexperienced do, who distort the limb: this is harmful, and such actions are foolish. I can only suggest leaving it alone or correctly treating it in its entirety.
des diverses manieres de brisure	regarding various methods of breaking up
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	Many ways of fractures exist, and various shapes, and their causes are determined;
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	For there are fractures caused by the impact of a sword, and the collar bone breaks up to the shaft at its junction with the bone, similar to a hatchet or staff strike; because this is how such a fracture is called, "hatchet break".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword penetrates through the bone from above without piercing it, and this is called a "complete" fracture; and the injuries caused by these two kinds of fractures are either large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is sequential impact, or crack, or break in the bone, or under a stone, or other similar occurrences.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a fracture up to the membrane that is under the bone or above it, and this wound can be large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if there is a wound that has gone into the bone as thin as a hair, and this crack is small, for this it is called this "hairline" fracture.
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound is made by striking with a stone or falling, or by any similar thing, and causes part of the bone to come out, resulting in the limbs being fractured as when candle-makers are working on the candles; similarly, the stone enters from within.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more with those who have soft bones, such as in children's bones.
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And it happens in all these ways of breaking that small fragments are evacuated as with shells; and I will speak about them in their order.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And let us know all methods of breaks through the removal above them, and the investigation on stakes, and by the putrid flesh which is upon.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of hair is known when one has uncovered the bone and rubbed inside it, revealing the dark break.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In treating a break, beware of adverse effects from the malady, and if you observe no harmful incident such as vomiting bile, loss of consciousness, extension, pallor, fever, and other symptoms appearing in various conditions, cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any alarming accidents, and you hope for salvation, then start the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when snow first comes to you, and it's in winter, then you should remove the bone before the fifteenth day since you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it's in summer, then hurry to remove the bone before the seventh day so that the pus under the bone may be rotten, and bring about the accidents we have mentioned.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues,	And if the bone fracture reaches up to the membrane covering the brain, you must cut into the fractured part in this way: and take hold of the skull from where the bone is broken, and expose as much of the bone as possible in every manner that you can, and further towards the shape of the wound more than you can.
et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	And when the flow of blood begins to uncover the bone, or an abscess forms, you must assist with what is necessary, and it is that you fill the body with moistened linen in rose oil.
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc .ij. manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And let the wound rest until the abscess pain subsides and there is enough flow of blood; then begin to excavate towards the bone, and it is done according to two methods: one method is that you cut in a narrow strip at the front, and this is the form:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then make another cut larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second way is that you have many different sizes of cuts, some narrow and others wide, and they should be pointed, and made of hard iron; and in operation lightly, so as not to wound the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is thick and hard, it is necessary that you pierce inside, in such a way that you perform cuts with needles, not so deep that they penetrate beyond the thickness of the flesh, and there should be a margin above the point about 1 inch, ensuring the point does not pass beyond the bone; and you must have several, so that each goes to its place under the thickness of the bone, having needles for all parts; and this is the form of the three ways of using needles:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality to pierce through the bone is that you place one needle on the bone, and turn with your hands until you know the bone is pierced. Then replace the needle a little later elsewhere, and do so throughout, then scrape out the space of the bone between the roots of teeth as precisely as possible, and do this more finely than you can, gently, as we have said, as long as you are able to remove the bone with your hands or any instruments you have like forceps, pliers; and make sure not to touch the brain or the sinus.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout .i. autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced and treated the bone, it is fitting that you reset the bone which has remained of the bone to all 1. another instrument similar to a canine tooth, but it should be more hardened and finer than the other canine tooth;
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a .i. des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	and if there is nothing of the small bones remaining, nor any scales, then reset them with 1. tools lightly; then treat the wound with the ointments and remedies that we have mentioned.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other method of treatment is as Galien said, which is safer; and it involves applying a strong lard, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	Firstly, you should uncover part of the bone, at or near where the break is made and moves, so when you have uncovered that part, place under the tip of this lens-shaped incision tool, as it's shown here.
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en .ij. costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	And do not cut from one side only, and the limb should be divided into two parts, so that when you cut you are directed towards the bone; then with a small hammer above, so that you strike lightly across the entire bone, and take great care of the mesh that is there;
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	If it's pushed towards the bone, gently push it, for you'll feel no harm with the bone, and no pain.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone fracture does not puncture until it touches the tissue and only the bone is cut from above, and there are small pieces left, then after that roughness, you should scrape off the scales with a fine shaver you must have various sizes, in order to apply the most suitable for each part according to the work and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you stand before great razors, and afterwards of finer tools, and do not stop doing this until it is done well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In every other haircutting and subtle breaking tasks, you should adjust the work according to its position; this is something that cannot be answered by someone who has devoted their study to this craft.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes .i. drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if it is discovered that the wound is bleeding, you should take one and a half pieces of linen cloth, according to the size of the wound, and soak them in rose oil, then apply them to the wound;
puis pren .i. autre drapeil doublé en .ij. ou en .iij., et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus .i. autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	Then take another piece of linen cloth, doubled either two or three times, and soak it in wine and rose oil, then place it over the first cloth; do this as lightly as you can so as not to weigh down the wound, then apply a second layer of string, but don't tighten it too much just enough so that it only touches the wound.
et le laisse ensi .i. jor ou .ij., tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	And let it do so for one or two days until the abscess drains, then dislocate it again and administer remedies such as roots of wormwood, flour of cloves, incense powder, and mustard seed, and similar things; make a powder from these and apply it to the wound, then give medications that reduce inflammation but are not painful.
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And ensure the wound is clean, do not leave any ointment nor allow any pus to assemble. For when pus assembles on the fabric of the brain, it circulates and causes harm, leading to great suffering for the patient. As one applies a pungent thing to the head, it disturbs from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take heed then, should any unfortunate events befall the patient as we have described, it is with doubt and without fear.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et .iij. parties d’oile roset et en glue .i. drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if no fear comes out only because of the medicine that we have placed on it, should this virtue be present, then you must take a part of honey, and three parts of rose oil and one part of beeswax glue, and spread it on the affected area;
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat with the appropriate treatments until you are healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that the two parts above the nose are never broken, or only one is broken if you do so, because they consist of two bones; and this lower part is cartilaginous, it doesn't break, nor does it weaken from twisting or bending, then heals.
Et se l’une des .ij. parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, then you must pinch your little finger or under the nose and apply an equal breakage inside to your index finger, and outward at the nostril hole, until the nose revives according to its natural shape;
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And do this gently, and watch that the patient does not feel pain through your operation.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is above the nose part and cannot reach to the place on the head, then it is necessary that you put it at an equal distance from the tip of a somewhat thick reed.
Et se li brisure est de .ij. pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the break is in two parts, redo the operation and try to restore it on the first day, if you can;
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	But if not, after the seventh or eighth day when the wound has calmed down, then bind to the tip of the nose with a linen gauze. If the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	If you pull two from another side, if breaking occurs; and let the threads be so thick that they fill the little hollows of the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor. Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	And say that a restorative should moisten the threads in butter and change each day. I do not think it is proper, but they should be moistened during the preparation of an omelette mixture with flour; then leave the thread until the bone becomes firm and the cartilage hardens.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes use goose feathers instead of threads, and if with one egg you cover the inside, and keep it warm, and blow into the wound, do whatever you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if the abscesses come to the nose in the same way as you handle them, put a wad of moistened wax or cotton in olive oil, or in a pot of snail juice.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if pus doesn't come out, then apply a plaster on the outside, made of sawdust and incense powder mixed with yolk oil. Then place light wafers on top, without tying them too tightly.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	And if the bones have been broken in small pieces and are thus fragmented, then use suitable tools for this task. Then open the wound, clean it with surgical procedures, and stitch, as you would apply bandages or salves suitable for such an area;
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is no injury within the nose, then perform a nasal treatment, and place cloves in it as long as it remains healthy.
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the rupture of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is fractured internally and there's no wound visible from the outside, and only the breakage is external, not shattered within. It doesn't crack into two halves but breaks internally, so it's easily recognized.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary; if the fracture occurs in the right part, you should press your index finger into the mouth near the jawbone. And if the fracture is in the left mandible, then use your right hand's index finger and press it gently into the inside of the injury, and do this with the other hand from the outside, making sure to do so evenly.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jaw is complete and affects both sides (.i.e., left and right), it is necessary that you administer an equal extension on both parts until they are even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And when the movements of the teeth occur, or a rupture, hold them with a thread of gold, silver, or silk. Then place on the broken jaw pieces of beeswax, and put under one doubled piece of cloth; then on the cloth put a large candle properly made, or a piece of leather equal in size to the length and width of the jaw. Secure it in such manner that you can, command the patient to rest, and eat small pieces of light meat.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see that the figure changes, then untie on the third day, and then adjust what has become undone; apply plaster, made with powder from a mill mixed generously with eggs or flour of almond meal, after removing the beeswax; then place under the plaster light wool, and if the plaster hardens, and the patient's position does not change, let it be for as long as they are healing. Many times heal in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if you encounter pus-filled sores, then follow what we have instructed many times.

And if you see the base of the stumps and constriction, as we have said, in the place that you restore the broken member, and you doubt about removing the abscess, if you leave it to bind until the seventh day, as we have said; then observe every three days the binding, making sure itching does not swell or come around the site where it was supposed to be drained, or the discharges do not come up to the limb because it is too constricted. If there's a mistake, as we have said.

And if no such incidents occur, or if the dislocation does not occur for two days or longer, and the patient rests with the ailment on his back, and has his hands on his stomach; and place under the shoulder one cloth filled equally with wool, and observe every hour of the day or night, making sure that the figure of the broken limb does not move, or that the bandages are softening; if it heals through the virtue of medicine, and gives him the meat we had placed before, in such a way that the meat is at first tender; and when he starts to recover, if it becomes bulky. de la brisure du bras	from the breaking of the arm
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is made up of two bones, which are called the "foscile" duo. One bone is small and serves the pocket; while the other is large, being this one underneath, towards the small two. By chance, only the large foscile breaks, or the small one, by chance they come together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble. Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	When the small fosciles break, restoration is easy and healing; but when the large ones break, the healing is bad, and worse than when they broke together. If it's only the small foscile that breaks, then gently stretching should suffice, and setting appropriately.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus .i. cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et .i. cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a .i. liien, et uns autres ministres a .i. autre au desus. Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And if it's the large foscile that breaks, you should pull more tightly; and stretch on one cushion, and adjust the pocket of your hand higher than the others, and the small finger lower than the other fingers, and make sure the patient crosses their own middle fingers, and another cushion in front them a little higher so they do not experience any discomfort. Then have the assistants extend their arms to the part below their hand, or at the elbow, and one helper on each side above that point. Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the breaking apart into pieces, you place each one in its own spot; and should there be none that gets caught with a bone, and you cannot return it to its spot, then proceed by making contact with the bone, as we have explained previously.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if in the process of healing from an injury, I spoke about it specifically in chapter singular; then take the treatment.

And if during the beginning of the restoration, ulcers occur, then apply this: Take one layer made of beeswax and white beeswax, ensuring it is neither too hard nor too soft; and place another layer by carefully joining them together, until the ulcers are soothed. Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer. Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if care is taken that no hardening should happen to the limb, because it is too confined, then it should be required that you soften it by rubbing, and leave thus for a few days, until the hardness disappears, and then tighten.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a .xx. jors. ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en .xxx. jors ou en .xxxv., et par aventure en .xx. jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus. de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	Regarding the fracture of the hand bone
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com .i. sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice .vij. jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of the womb is broken, if it causes it to swell, then place her upright, lean her towards the lower back part and keep her rearward. And when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and after she's done, put her back in place. Do this for seven days or more: the break will be healed. If you see fit, take a goat bladder, tie a stick at its opening, fill the bladder into nature; then blow forcefully through the stick until the bladder is inflated inside. Nature would heal from that break. Afterwards fill it with cotton and let it sit like this for some days, till it heals properly.

de brisure avec plaie	Of breaking with wound
