Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is healing, you can apply vitriol to it, and if there's no other option, then continue to try restoring the broken bone in that same hour or day, or on that day, should abscesses not form.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if abscesses do form, let the treatment continue for another day, until the abscess is relieved, and don't disturb it on the third or fourth day either, as you would be causing harm with that.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if you see the bone has broken out from under its skin, it is necessary that you place it gently in your hands, with a slight extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the limbs don't allow you to place them evenly in your hands, then use this iron tool with it, which is made of iron and has a length of seven or six inches, and its width should match the size of the wound; for each fracture treatment, the surgeon must have three or four of these tools according to his need; they should be round and slightly thick, so that they don't bend under compression on your limb when you work, and they should be sharp in front, and rounded in the middle towards the front.
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre. Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And it is called "palainche", so that the crooked bones should be placed on the exposed part of the bone; and use it once, until you see results, and ensure they are even against each other. And if the fracture is subtle, and the tools cannot grasp the bone well, then hold the head of the bone as long as the tools can handle it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you can't return the bone back, as we have said, if you have an instrument suitable for this purpose, or a scalpel or surgeon's knife, in your power; then cut into the bone that is stuck within it with roughness and small shavings.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil. Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille .i. drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	And when the bone is returned and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it's not in its natural place. If you have to ensure it's in place, then apply a mixture of one part red wine and stoptic black powder and clean it properly if possible; and don't put any paste or other thing with oil on the wound as it might cause gangrene and decay. Then administer these when you've restored the bone, let the wound be uncovered, and cover it completely according to its size, and ensure that the wound is not strained by breaking. Many have done this carelessly and caused death or corrosion in the patient at times; and so make sure the tightening of the wound isn't with broken pieces. And many have treated this way, causing death or corrosion in various instances; and let the pressures be softer and more consistent than other breaks.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie. Et quant tu vois aprés .i. jor ou .ij. enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that harmful incidents might occur, as we have said before, and you find pain in the area, then it's not advisable to apply treatments; but wrap it tightly instead. If after one or two days you notice an improvement on the wound, remove what you had applied with all the wine and replace it with a healing ointment, such as the tetra-formula ointment or similar products.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary for you to dislocate the limb twice a day, in the morning and at vespers, until it is healed and sound.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary for the limb to be bandaged in such a way that the joint slides easily.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if the days pass and it cannot heal anymore right away, know that there are small pieces of bone causing this, so it is necessary for you to treat the wound with a tent, and remove all these pieces causing discomfort, which bring about pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant. Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés .xx. jors ou .xxx., puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And if a fistula comes about in the wound or some other form of corruption, it is necessary to treat it according to what he instructed before in this chapter. And when bone is broken and exposed within the limb, such as the bone of the elbow or shoulder, and others like them on the larger limbs; do not treat it immediately because many times death results from it. But let it decay until it putrefies; perhaps after 20 days or 30 days, then you can heal the wound if possible; but if you cannot, leave it alone.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	The blows that come from sweat
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	The blows come many times after the healing of the wound, especially when it's near the joint. And there is much to see in the shape of the limb; and by chance cannot perform its natural actions on the limb.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care therefore when it comes to such things: if you give him/her stiffening medicines such as aloes, frankincense, and myrrh, sarsaparilla, senna, and similar others, do so according to which of these you choose or all together, mixing them with stinking wine or enough eggs or milk; then apply them on the knot in poultices, press well and don't remove it with your hands day by day; then reset it, and start again another one until the knots are removed. Or apply pressure onto a piece of wood well made; because the properties of wood is such that it removes all swellings from the limbs; and if the knot has hardened into hardness like stone and needs to be removed, cover it with a bandage, showing the excessness clearly visible; or take it off to any barber until it's removed, then continue the treatment until healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	Of the limb that is weak after the siege
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the breaking of the bone is restored, and after that the limbs are weak and delicate, it happens for many reasons: because one was tied too tightly and wasn't tied as it should have been; or because there were too many bandages, and they couldn't breathe properly on the limb; or due to excessive swelling; or due to too large movements not in their time; or because he lacks blood in his body, being weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the treatment is that you make the patient eat the herbs, and make their body soft until the swelling multiplies within them; then give them baths, and bring them joy and rest. Afterward, apply grease to the limb so that the grease attracts to the major swelling, and wash it often with lukewarm water until the swelling aligns with the limb; and restore its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	If a limb is bent after an injury.
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limbs are twisted after being put back in place, and if the bones have been broken apart, and though the shape of the limb is distorted, it does not lose its natural function: do not believe those who say that one must break the entire limb anew; many such actions are done in our land. These practices are criticized and result in severe harms and even death; however, when the swelling and pain are still fresh, they should be treated with hot water or with herbs that soften tissue, like mint leaves, roots, and thyme, etc.; and one should apply a moistening plaster, such as well-made duck fat, and take the essence of mint and mix it with lard or oil from sesame, then make a plaster. Alternatively, take greased figs and grind them with cornmeal and similar medicines that reduce inflammation.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes. Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And without fail, massage the dislocation with wet hands continuously and for an extended period. And allow the limb to move every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the twisting is hardened and durable, like bone, and requires being treated with metal, so that it reaches up to the bone, one should do this gently at the precise point of incision. And include consideration and study in the treatment process.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	This begins the book on dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, because it cannot move there anymore, and the limb is incorrectly positioned, causing great pain and injury to the body.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation happens without any reason, if it fits now to bring back without disturbing anything.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	For if one delays, the joints swell up, and by chance one might put them back to their places; because it is not suitable to move him when his joints are swollen: many times caused pain and other aches;
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	When such a situation occurs, if you have a surgeon for the patient, then let them continue, until all abscesses are relieved; then immerse the limb in hot water and oil, then gently reset it, and treat each limb according to where treatment would naturally come.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have organized the chapters on shoulder dislocations up to this point.
des mandibules	of the jaws
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	Sometimes the jaws are dislocated downwards, and the dislocations of both occur in two ways: either they are somewhat connected to their places and slightly softened; or they are completely dislocated, hanging towards the chin, and causing saliva from the mouth not to be contained, nor able to close his mouth, and wrapping his tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When a dislocation is small, it can return through various arrangements.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it is complete and accomplished, you should reset it quickly without hesitation.
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de .ij. pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And in such a way that the attendant cuts off the patient's head, and pushes his fingers into his cheek pouch with one of her hands at the root of the jaw dislocation inside the mouth, if the dislocation is .ij. parts; and the other hand should be out from between them for equality; and command the patient to soften his jaws, and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the fingers are kept equally placed until it regains its position in place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if returning it causes pain, similarly when these two jaws are together, using hot water and oil, as long as gently resetting them; do not overly force the reset, just as we said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they are returned evenly, and the mouth of the patient feels well after being moistened, then place damp cloths as poultices made from oil roset and beeswax, then bind them lightly with soft threads.
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre .ij. cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	And let the patient sleep on their back, and have their shoulders lying between two cushions, so that they don't move nor to the right nor to the left, but do not strain themselves too much, instead they should eat light meat until the pains are alleviated, and secure the jaws.
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And then taste this to have it taken lightly, and does not struggle to open the mouth for eating and drinking until the jaw is well set and healed.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be properly set in one hour and are not returned to their original position, they lead to fevers and chronic discomfort, and by chance stomach release, and by chance vomiting of pure contents.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is a loss; and many times death befalls the one to whom it happens, within eight days.
de la forcelle	from the lever principle
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The strength cannot relieve from within the continuation of it and from its back, and is dislocated only once outside, and one feels this well indeed.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	And the restoration is such that the patient lies on his back and extends his arms; and then presses onto the lesion forming to your palm, and it will return; then place on the plaster and cover it with a bandage, and it will be held.
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	And the head that is towards the blade cannot be resetted; if it does not, and if it gets reset once, then you must reset it to its place as we have said; then place on the plaster and cover with a bandage, and tighten it, and instruct the patient to rest until they are sane.
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And similarly, the shoulder blades are brought back when it is removed from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc .iij. manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	Know that the shoulder is dislocated in three ways: one way is when it dislocates at the part of the socket below; and the second is at the part under the heel; and by chance dislocates at the top part, which happens rarely;
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	And it does not dislocate behind the shoulder, nor inside through the nerves; and several times dislocates near the socket, especially in those with little flesh, for then it springs quickly out of place; for those with enough flesh, it jumps to points and returns by them.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes happens to some men due to percussion or cracking, and the shoulder swells with an inflamed abscess, and they think that it is dislocated from this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Thus, you must verify it as long as you are certain about it; then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And when you recognize a dislocation as it moves towards the collarbone, and makes a distinction between the diseased shoulder and the healthy one, you will find their clear difference.
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	You will find a hollow at the top of the shoulder. From the collarbone to the armpit, the peak of the shoulder is like that of an 'O'; and it cannot allow the patient to bring their hand to their nose or move in any manner.
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	And also, if it is dislocated at the top and not completely hidden, because you clearly find it at the armpit.
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And this method of dislocation can only be remedied when it is new or if it's caused by illness.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is: the surgeon raises his hand above the illness, then places his fingers on the elbow and lifts the joint to full height at the top of the body; and the surgeon raises his hand and extends it upwards, then puts it under; if it comes too quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	And if it does not come as we have said in our hands for several days, then the sick person should be bathed in warm water; and he or she should be treated with soothing warmth and relief, such as decoction of garlic and fenugreek and melilot in water, and it should be treated.
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	Then wrap the sick person's back with it, and place a pad of even thickness on the elbow. Don't make it too soft or too hard. Then place the heel on the pad, and lift the shoulder blade up properly, and guide the hand towards the illness.
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	And one other surgeon cuts the skin of the patient's back, so that it does not move downwards; this shoulder comes back completely now, and if you see if you reset it according to this manner:
et est que tu faices estre present .i. home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	And it is that you make present .i. at home something bigger than the patient; and keep it straight towards the body side, and bend the shoulder against the back of the patient, and raise the back in high place so that the back hangs down in a row;
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre. Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And another surgeon pulls the hand of the patient towards the back and towards the belly. And if the patient is too light, then push something heavy with him, and the dislocation will return now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche .i. lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com .i. pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	And to reset it in another way: and one should stick a long stick into the ground, so that the head is placed as well as with a bullet, and not too big or too slippery;
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	Then place it above the wound, but so that it has a sheet under it, and while the wound is long like the stick; then extend your hand below on the other side in form, and the joint will return to its place quickly.
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren .i. tison de .ij. bras de grant et .iiij. dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	and if it does not return through all these things that we have said, then do this cure: take one wrist of two strong and four fingers wide, which has the head rounded to be able to enter almost straight into the socket, according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	then tie it on the top of the stick with a sheet underneath, so that the stick does not irritate the wound; then place it onto the socket towards the wound; and extend your arm up to the stick from its tip, and fix the shoulder support onto the stick, and the arm at the base of the hand, then put the arm down on one pole as long as half a span wide, and let the other hand hang down now; the joint will return in this position.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is so, no matter how, should you need to place upon the joint a thread that's even, then apply plastered with powdered mill grain, along with incense and yolk of egg, across all the shoulder and around it, then remove from the joint addition, and tie back on the plaster, and wrap the hand in its neck. And let your hands stay like this.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it should be that he eats a little, until the limbs are strengthened, for it will heal more quickly; and then eat more after five days or seven, and move them; and if it is firm and not softened, it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a iij. pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is loose due to moisture that caused it or for another reason, you should apply three hot cauteries to it, as was detailed in the chapter about cauteries before.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and it dislocates after seven days, and the joint doesn't stay in place, and can't lift your arm upwards, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is damaged or extended or weakened; and know that the joint would never be properly fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Dislocations that are near the buttocks and breasts, or behind, if caused by pushing and stretching of hands, are administered in other places; treatment should be applied as long as it remains clean.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing there comes stiffness in the limb, and late movements, then apply hot baths many times, until that stiffness is relieved, and returns to its first nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	Of the shoulder joint's dislocation
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the shoulder is dislocated at points and returns to these points; and if it has been dislocated from all directions, equally in front and behind, then dislocation cannot be fully restored, for you can see this clearly and feel it well; and it is dislocated according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement. Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	And when you join the shoulder bone with the healthy side, if you can see it clearly. For the joint is bony, and cannot bend the arm or touch its shoulder in any way.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary to reset it in this way that the abscesses are close to heal, because if they were healed too quickly, it would be a problem to bring them back; and sometimes cannot be brought back completely, even when it's behind; it is worse than other dislocations, and causes more pain, and in consequence death may come.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is like this when one can return it to its normal state: you extend your patient's hand with both of yours; and his arms are spread outwards and downwards, and his hands are placed in front according to the length of the forearm, forwards, backwards, and sideways, then you push the joint towards his wrist area or at the base of his palm until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, then it returns when he holds both his hands together, and pushes with the base of his palm against the knife that is stuck out.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	And if it does not return to its place, then apply strong extension; and when both persons assist in extending the arm, and they press against the extended arm with their hands, so that it doesn't move during extension. Then turn the arm from each side, once you have wrapped a long and wide cloth around it;
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	And when you touch the joint to its place with your hand, if you smear some oil on it to soften the joint, then press and shape the joint until it heals;
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And when it's in place, put some dry plaster with yolk of egg on it and press it until it heals; then stretch the arm towards the neck gently, and leave it there for some days, then release.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firmly in its place, remove the bandage and let it be; and if you see that the joint isn't set well, redo the plaster and the bandage, and leave it like that for some days, until it's firmly set; then release.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse .i. jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	And if it feels sore after the setting of the joint, and it moves again, wash and rub it well, pressing until it's relieved; or you apply a layer of fatty sheep fat to the joint, then leave it for one day and night, then give him a bath;
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai .ij. fois ou .iij., tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And when it sweats, rub the joint carefully, then place it on ice, and then dip in water; and do this twice or three times until he is well; and if you see fit, apply wet calf fat with butter to it, and apply it; should return to its position.
li dislocation de la main	the dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The hand's dislocated joint decreases gradually, more than other joints. When it happens, one should immediately bring it back to its original position during the dislocation itself, so that the limbs swell up or an abscess occurs.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	And for bringing it back, you should place the arm on a board and extend the assistant's hand, then place your own hand evenly so that your palm is in line with the appearance of the joint, and hold it until it recovers.
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	Always, you must check if it's perfectly in place; then have the patient lie on their back with one hand supported on a table during extension and retraction.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele aparance de la jointure. S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	And if the dislocation is in the back of the hand, have the patient lie on their back with the back of their hand on the table, and place their hand on the appearance of the joint. If it returns now, it's correctly done.
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If not, if the pressure bandages for abscesses heal, and then leave it so without starting over.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	And if he cannot bear it, and you can't put him in place after a few days, then the joint will remain twisted;
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And it does no harm to the patient as long as your hands are moistened and cannot strain anything completely: then you know that the nerve is cut, or the artery; if there's no other way except to apply a cautery when necessary, and perhaps in that case nothing else matters.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when your hands are ready, if you place on the plaster that we have mentioned, then strain it and leave it for five days, then release it and leave it like that.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you can't move it well, and there's no fracture, then apply warm water, and rub it until it is clean.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	From the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;	The fingers of the hand are never displaced individually, neither on the back of the palm nor on the underside.
adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;	So the fingers are kept together, and the dislocation is confined to those joints until they heal. Then support the head of the finger, and bend it towards the part where it was separated.
et le laisse .ij. jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit,	And leave it for two days, then set it straight on the third day; and don't let it move, as we have said, and the dislocation will heal on that day. Bend the finger again, and let it move, and reapply the bandage later; and repeat this process until it is properly aligned.
et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	And do the same if it dislocates at the wrist, and do like you did before until it stops hurting; and do the same when it dislocates elsewhere.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	With ankle dislocation or back.
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the ankle, back or neck is dislocated, or if there are multiple dislocations, without any treatment, for the pain overwhelms the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les .ij. cuixes ou li dui bras ou .j.	And the symptoms are that the patient's bodily functions lose control and cannot be held back, and many times parts of their body soften, or both knees or either two arms or one.
Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a iiij. pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	And many times, it becomes two parts; that which becomes behind is called "gibbousness".
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	The treatment is to reward when the gibbousness has come from childhood: if there is no treatment or healing at all.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit;	And that which comes from falling, strikes or similar things, according to the old methods of treatment by great words, it doesn't bring any great benefit in all respects;
mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	but I have summarized it according to my intention, and I have formed tools in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit;	I say that when the illness comes to the breast before it reaches the belly, there is no harm or sickness;
et ausi cele que vient droitement en .ij. costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis;	And also this that comes straight to the two ribs, and we cannot cure from anything other than what directly affects the back, as I say;
et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en .i. leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece;	And it is that the illness spreads over his belly up to one span evenly, and has some tension beneath him, so he does not blister;
puis fiche .i. tison au chief en terre forment, et .i. autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et .i. autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles;	Then place one ember at his head on the earth forming, and another at the elbows, and tie a band beneath the spots of the illness, and another at the hips, and knees, and ankles;
et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les .ij. tisons;	And two surgeons know how to tie them, one at the head and others at the points, among these two stakes;
et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	And be sure they are well closed, the stake as we have said, and the mirror place her palms on the spine form until she regains consciousness.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de .iij. bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee;	And if she doesn't recover from this treatment, take a board of one and a half the length of a man's body, and place it over the body, and if the wounds are on the side, place the head of the board over the wound, then put the middle of the board on the spine;
et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And have the mirror place her feet on the other end of the board, press well until she regains consciousness at her head; and if you see it happening to the elbow that turns toward the hand, do it there.
Et est que tu fiches .ij. tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez .ij. autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc;	And you should place two needles into the head of the patient's arm from large ends to small ones, and on either side of the bones two others, with each needle in between them spaced about a palm's length.
et ait en chescun tison .i. pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns .ij. tisons ait .i. tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en .ij. tornans .ij. petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	And in each needle place one piece of bone or the joint socket, and ensure that the needles are firmly set into the ground so they don't move; and between every two needles place another twisted needle, since this is how the bones turn, and for turning the joint, have a pair of small needles about the length of a palm.
et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And then join the ligament located among the muscles at the joint towards the head and the other ligament toward the bones at the opposite joint; and each of the servants turns their joints to all parts of the ligament, while the masters place the spine evenly as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de .iij. dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when they are even, if you put on desiccating plaster with plenty of egg white, and then apply bandages, and then cover them with a tablet of one and three-quarters inches long, which protects the area of the gallbladder and the healthy part of the spine, then bind it with a string, as we have said, and allow the patient to move subtly until they are healed.
et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc,	And if nothing comes at the end of recovery, then it is necessary to administer softening and soothing medicines, with the tablet we mentioned previously; and each time it is administered there should be a piece of ghee.
et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And if any appearance comes at the bottom of the spine in the back, take care that it is a dislocation; and it's the bone that opens up, so one should not have presumption about this: it might bring death.
des dislocations de la hainche	Dislocations of the hip
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Know that the joints of the hip and shoulder only suffer dislocations, unlike other joints; and the hip joint is dislocated according to four parts: inside and outside, front and back; and more inside, somewhat dislocated in front and behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	And the knowledge of such dislocation from inside is that when one joins the diseased leg with the healthy one, it becomes longer and allows the diseased knee to open more than the healthy one, and prevents the diseased knee from bending backwards.
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And it is where the legs are swollen due to an abscess, because the hip bone comes into contact with them.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of one who approaches death, if it is that this event is contrary to these before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of one who approaches before [death], if it is that his leg is well according to completion; nevertheless, he does not even double the knee without pain, and if you want to make him walk, he cannot do so beforehand, and he retains his urine, and swells up the ankle, and when he walks, he goes on tiptoe.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of one who approaches behind [death], if it is that he cannot spread his knee, nor double it, and this leg is more bent than the other, and the ankle becomes soft, and the shoulder of the hip moves under the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The remedy for this appearance of dislocation is that you should confirm whether the dislocation is old and stays in its position, if there is no treatment; and it does not benefit to assume anything.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And for those in which the dislocation is recent, there are four ways of dislocation, if you hurry to correct it and stretch inside and outside, and move to the right and left; should it return successfully, requiring no other treatment afterwards.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles .i. ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a .ij. mains, ou a .i. liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil;	And if it doesn't return this way, you should apply one strong remedy, and firmly hold the leg with both hands, or tie at one point above the knee;
et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien;	And apply other remedies by extending your hand above in such a way that it presses the hands against the buttocks, then pull it with one strong tug at the knee; and hold the head with another at the tie.
et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And stretch up and down at once all together, until the patient is lifted from the ground at once, and remains hanging.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This way of stretching is common for four similar situations, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is correct.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance. Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele;	But if not, then you should treat it according to its appearance. When the dislocation is in the pardedens (a part of the thoracic cavity), you need to lift the patient onto their healthy side, then tie them up at the base of the foot, and above the ribcage, then lift the bandage towards the chest area and towards the strength.
puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	Then take hold of another assistant for their arms, and embrace the large part of the diseased foot, and extend it upwards in this form: if it returns to its position now; and this way of dislocation is lighter than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les .ij. piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les .ij. talons, et sus les .ij. genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue .ij. dois plus que li autres;	And if you cannot compress it in this way as we have said, then you should bind the two feet together with a strong bandage below each foot and around both knees, and make sure that the bad leg extends two fists longer than the other one;
puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre .ij. bras de lonc; puis comande a .j. ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	Then have it hung from the head of a post, and two feet above the ground about half the length; then instruct one minister to encircle the head of the thigh, and another ministers are hanging with the bad side, who should encircle firmly the thigh, for the joint is now returning quickly.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne .i. liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi;	And when dislocation occurs at the front, if you place the bad leg as we have said in those with elasticity, and stretch a band properly on the bad leg and even on the foot.
puis met .ij. tisons, .i. au chief et .i. autre as piez, puis fiche .i. tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme;	Then place two needles, one on the head and the other on the toe, then insert one needle between the buttocks of the patient in the form;
et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	and place damp cloths around it, so as not to blister the patient, then have each doctor extend themselves towards him, and you should set the dislocated part in line with his hand.
S’elle revient, c’est boin. Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If it returns, that's good. If not, place him on a table, and press him down in such a way as we have said in the context of gilbositis, and lie the patient on his healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it's necessary to extend the affected leg quickly, and according to what I have said; and make the patient feel their pain on the side of the affected shoulder, then press with the other hand, and pull forward towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les .ij. hainches;	And if the dislocation is at the back, then it does not require stretching of the body below or lifting off the ground, instead it should be placed as when the hip was dislocated backward, just like we said about lying on both hips.
et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table;	And be at its face, and the neck stretched as we previously described, it must apply pressure to the joint on the table;
et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve;	And it will be right when the limbs extend their legs, and they are equal; therefore adjust the hips, and place the plaster, and apply pressure with a belt, so that the hip does not move;
et se repose .iij. jors ou .iiij., puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse. iij. jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And let it rest for three days or four, then release it, and place the plaster again; and if you see that they are equal, apply pressure in the same way as before, and leave it for three more days; then release it, and move him around properly until the limb is strengthened.
de la dislocation dou genoil	From the dislocation of the shoulder joint
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The shoulder joint can be dislocated in three ways: this means, inside and outside, and behind; and it does not dislocate in front.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez;	And the signs for this are that you instruct the patient to bend their leg at the knee, and if they cannot straighten it at the knee, know that it is dislocated.
et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez;	And the restoration of all this is that you have the patient sit up straight, and extend their leg if they can, and place your back against their buttocks, and put their foot on yours.
puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les .ij. costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement;	Then take his kidney between your palms and withdraw it between your fingers, then bend the two sides of the kidney form. And another attendant extends his foot until the knee returns to its place, and the signs are that he has bent his leg lightly towards his thigh.
et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort .iij. jors ou iiij., puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	and place the bandage on it, and let the leg rest at the thigh, and hold them together strongly for three or four days, then let him move around; and do not allow any work to affect the wounds, until the limbs are strengthened.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the limbs are not yet right, administer vigorous stretching, as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	Regarding the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels are never completely reset and still remain in or out.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee:	And the signs of this are that the ankle swells up, and moves forward towards the part where it is dislocated:
li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	The reduction (or resetting) is easy, and you should gently extend it with your hands only when it's properly aligned.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne .i. ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville;	And when it is dislocated from all sides, it must be that you make the patient stand straight, and hold them with two assistants by their leg, above the ankle;
puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre .ij. fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut;	then draw the foot towards you with your right hand, and then also to the left four times, then lift them up, and firmly support the foot upwards;
et fai ce .ij. fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient;	and do this twice, as we have said, by gripping and pulling the foot; if it returns, that's well; if not, start the process again, for it will return.
et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche .i. passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide;	and if it cannot return this way, lay the patient on their back to the ground, and place a stone firmly into the earth between their buttocks, and bind them tightly with cloths, so as not to hurt the patient.
puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a .i. liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet;	Then doctors rub his feet, and some other doctors stretch out the leg up to his hands or up to two inches, he holds it on the neck of the leg;
puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent;	Then extend each doctor equally, and let the assistant be placed between the feet of the patient to hold the patient when stretching them.
puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	Then place the mirrors equally at the dislocated joints with your hands, and some other doctors cut the healthy leg above the knee, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois;	And when it is at the right point, apply the dressing and fasten it with bandages, then tighten properly, and bind the leg to the thigh, and guard the nerves that are behind the ankle, so that the bandage does not become too tight.
puis le laisse .ij. jors ou .iij., et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par .iiij. jors;	Then leave it for 2 or 3 days, and if the joints are loose, hold them in place; then release it on the third day or fourth, and gradually tell the patient to move after four days;
et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And if he proceeds beyond this period, it is not a certainty that he will no longer dislocate.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you find pus coming out, then it is necessary to soothe it, as we have said elsewhere, until it heals.
des dois	This seems like an incomplete line or a typo in the original text. It would be "dois" which means 'two' in Old French, but without context, I can't provide a precise translation for this line. The full sentence might have been something along the lines of: "Dois jours" (Two days), though that doesn't fit perfectly with the surrounding sentences either.
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the shoulders are dislocated, if they need to be beautifully extended due to work, it's a light matter.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus .i. leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne;	And when the dislocation is neither in the buttocks nor behind the foot, it's necessary that you make the patient lie on .i. his entire back or on .ie. a table straight up, and place your foot where the joints open, then press firmly with your foot until it recovers;
et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a .ij. chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse .iij. jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when it's even and there is nothing opening, put under the foot's sole a table for two shoulders, then press firmly, and let him rest for three days, then reset him; and have him rest until he has recovered.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	regarding wounds and dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	When injury accompanies dislocation and one seeks to restore it, many times the patient dies:
si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis;	If you are not presumptuous in the treatment, if you lack wisdom in this art and have not practiced it for a long time, and if you are not compassionate and merciful but rather sluggish, do not engage.
et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit;	And start with calming things by draining pus, and leave the patient in God's hands, if you do not see any hope for recovery.
et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne;	And when you see hope, then reset the limb to its place, in such a way that the pus drains and heals.
et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis;	And when the limbs are in place, administer soothing remedies for abscesses and incisions, and treat the wound accordingly, using dried ointments.
et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples;	And if there is fracture along with dislocation, and small bones are broken, mend them, and do what we have advised for simple diseases.
et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors. Amen	And be careful not to fall into fear, according to what I've said, for this is done according to your Creator's will, and with the knowledge of you and your body. Amen.
